she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說 , 做她正在做的事是有幫助的 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	我非常興奮地見到她 , 看到一個例子 , 說明年輕人被賦予權力 , 能採取行動 , 讓世界變得更好 , 真的是我們未來的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜柯恩分享了一些關於塑膠污染的艱難事實 , 關於如何將自己從塑膠垃圾漩渦中解放 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色任務藍色、海洋、塑膠等 ,
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜柯恩:關於塑膠污染的強烈事實 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在用塑膠袋做塑膠袋 , 我剪斷和縫合 , 做為我藝術作品的主要材料 , 花了二十年 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二維三維的零件 , 雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	在與塑膠合作後 , 大約八年後 , 我的一些作品開始分裂 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	它和我們一樣是短暫的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在我對塑膠的進一步學習之後 , 我發現這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	不好的是 , 塑膠會分解成小塊 , 因為它一直都是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 很多是在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾處理器和健身房 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應是 , 我認為這是很多人對這件事的第一反應是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得走出去把這東西清乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我真的提出了一個提案 , 帶著一艘貨物船 , 以及兩艘退役的捕魚拖網漁船、一座起重機、一台晶片機器 , 以及一台冷模機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是去健身房 , 提高人們對這個議題的認知 , 開始將塑膠晶片切成碎片 , 冷藏成磚塊 , 可能是用來當建材在開發中社區的建築材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和實際去過健身房的人談話 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 很快地 , 我就意識到 , 清理這些塑膠垃圾 , 會比世界上每天製造的量來得少 , 且我得要回頭看更大的照片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的情況是:我們需要找到一個方法來關掉水龍頭 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要減少單一使用和丟棄的塑膠 , 它們每天都要進入海洋環境 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	看著這個 , 我也意識到我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只擔心塑膠在太平洋中間我所學到的現在已經有11個環流遍佈全球五大洋的塑膠垃圾
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	我不只關心塑膠垃圾 , 也關心超市的塑膠垃圾 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都是用塑膠包裝的 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都是用塑膠包裝的 , 甚至在健康食品市場也一樣 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也很關心冰箱裡的塑膠還有從塑膠滲出的有毒物質滲入我們體內
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群人一起研究這個問題 , 我們建立了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有很多計畫要進行 , 但其中有些很基本 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果我們發現海洋中百分之八十到九十的碎片是塑膠 , 那我們就稱之為 「 塑膠 」 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人的書都結束了他們關於永續和綠化的書籍 , 用回收的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放進一個桶子裡 , 你就不用再去想了 。
what is the reality of that ?	現實情況是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 塑膠回收率不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的去看它 , 特別是在塑膠瓶的時候 , 大部分塑膠瓶只會下循環、焚燒 , 或運到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被降級回收 , 變成更小的東西 , 而玻璃瓶可以再次成為玻璃瓶 , 或者再次使用塑膠瓶 , 永遠不會再是塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們在看且要求人們去思考的事情是 , 我們在 「 減少、再利用、回收 」 的前面加上第四個環節 , 三項是拒絕的 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	盡可能拒絕使用單一和丟棄的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些是很古老的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在正在收集這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 用它們來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為我自己和我的家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	要找到一個不銹鋼瓶、玻璃瓶 , 很容易 , 如果你要去旅行 , 且你忘了帶著不銹鋼瓶裝水或過濾水 , 和購買塑膠瓶的瓶裝水比較 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我想在這裡對大家說 , 我知道你們對這個問題了解很多 , 這個問題在海洋中是個大問題 , 但這是我們以消費者身份所創造出來的問題 , 我們可以解決 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以解決這個問題 , 做法是提高對這個問題的認知 , 並教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 盡可能選擇單用塑膠的替代方案 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這些流行病的根源切成海洋 , 這樣就能拯救我們的海洋、拯救我們的地球、拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這個示範來自麻省理工學院的帕蒂梅斯實驗室 , 由帕納•梅瑞推出 , 他是ted的推特 。 這是一個可穿戴的裝置 , 上面有一個投影機 , 用來為我們和環境的深切互動鋪路 。 想像 「 少數民族報告 」 , 然後一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	展示、設計、界面設計、科技 。
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	pattiemaes和pranvidemo第六感
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直對這個問題很感興趣:我們能否進化或發展出第六感 , 能否讓我們無縫接觸、容易取得資訊 , 或現存資訊 , 來協助我們做出正確的決定 , 決定我們即將遇到的狀況 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	有些人可能會說 , 現今的手機不就已經做到了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說 , 不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted遇見某人時 , 當然 , 這是最棒的網路平台 , 你不會和某人握手 , 然後說: 「 你能停下來一會兒嗎 ? 我拿出手機和google搜尋你 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或是當你到超級市場站在那個大型的衛生紙走道上時 , 你不會拿出你的手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 去一個網站 , 試著決定這些不同的衛生紙當中哪一種是最環保的購買方式 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以我們無法輕易取得這些相關資訊 , 來協助我們做出最佳決策 , 決定下一步該做什麼 , 以及該採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組正在研發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能用一種簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是要揭露我們最近的努力 , 目前為止 , 大部分的努力仍然在進行中 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	我現在正戴著這個裝置 , 把它們和貨架上的零件拼湊在一起 , 順便說一下 , 目前只需花350美金 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著一台攝影機 , 一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜式、電池動力的投影系統 , 裡面有一面鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件在我的口袋裡 , 向我的手機通訊 , 扮演著通訊和計算裝置的角色 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕納•密特里 , 他真的是執行和設計整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們可以看到這個系統讓他走到任何平面上 , 開始用他的手和投影在他面前的資訊進行互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	這個系統會追蹤這四個重要的手指 。
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著你可能認得的簡單標記帽子 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要一個比較時髦的版本 , 你也可以用不同顏色的指甲油漆上顏色 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上追蹤這四隻手指 , 識別他做任何的動作 , 例如 , 他可以直接去看長灘的地圖 , 放大縮小等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也能辨識出具代表性的手勢 , 比如 「 拍一張照片 」 手勢 , 接著拍一張你面前的任何東西的照片 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以走到任何一面牆上 , 投射所有他拍攝的照片 , 分類並整理它們 , 等等 , 使用所有自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	兩年前 , 在座有些人可能有來這裡看過傑夫•漢的示範 , 有些人可能會想: 「 這不是看起來像微軟的平面桌子嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用自然的手勢互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	差別在於 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面上 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西是可以取得的 , 和這些投影的資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是可以隨身攜帶的 , 可以是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	其中一個重要的差異是 , 它完全是行動裝置 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的差異是 , 明天的大量生產 , 成本不會比現在的手機還要多 , 且實際上 , 包裝的成本不會更大 , 可能會比我脖子上戴的這個版本看起來更模糊 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但除了讓你們其中一些人實現幻想在 「 少數報告 」 中看起來和湯姆克魯斯一樣酷 , 我們之所以對這個裝置感到非常興奮 , 是因為它真的可以作為第六感裝置之一 , 它可以給你有關你面前事物的資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到帕納走進超級市場 , 他在購買一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一個產品時 , 這個系統可以辨識出他拿到的產品 , 使用影像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以尋求額外的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以 , 在他的個人標準下 , 這個選擇是特別好的選擇 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	在座有些人可能想用最白化的廁所紙 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他可以拿亞馬遜的評分 , 投影在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是朱安的書 , 我們先前的講者 , 順道一提 , 在亞馬遜取得了很棒的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納翻閱了這本書的頁面 , 再看看書中讀者留言的額外資訊 , 像是他最喜歡的評論家所寫的 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他翻到某個特定的頁面 , 他會找到我們朋友的註解 , 給予他更多資訊 , 關於那一頁的任何東西 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙時 , 它永遠不會過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以得到你正在讀到的事件的影片註解 , 你可以得到最新的運動分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這個比較有爭議性 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted和某人互動時 , 也許你能看到一個字雲的標籤 , 和那個人在他們的部落格和個人網頁中聯繫在一起的字詞 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機感興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的航班延遲了 , 登機門也改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道現在是什麼時候 , 就跟在你的手臂上畫一支手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前在發展第六感時所在 , 能讓我們無縫接觸到關於我們可能遇到的事物的相關資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 像我說的 , 他是這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他確實應該得到很多掌聲 , 因為我認為他過去三個月沒睡多少 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友大概也對他不太滿意 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但它還不是完美的 , 它是一項進展 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 或許再過十年 , 我們將帶著大腦植入終極第六感來到這裡 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	在2001年9月11日 , 埃克韋菲被殺害了 , 死於不可思議的損失 。 rodriguez的兒子在世界貿易中心遭到攻擊 ; elwaf的兒子zacariamoussaoui被定罪於那些攻擊中 , 並且期盼能找到一個生命的句子 。 rodriguez的兩個媽媽已經知道並尊重另外一個 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治 。
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11療癒:那些找到原諒、友誼的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲利斯•羅德里格斯:今天我們在這裡 , 是因為我們有大多數人認為不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	但 , 現在感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次得知我的兒子在世界貿易中心在2001年9月11日的早上 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否死了 , 直到36小時後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治性的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家要以我們的兒子之名 , 以我的丈夫 , 奧蘭多 , 我和家人的名義 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它時 , 卻驚訝不已 , 驚恐的震驚 , 和我們生活中可怕的爆炸 , 真的是 , 我們沒有報復 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾週後 , zacariasmoussaoui被指控六項恐怖主義陰謀 , 美國政府要求對他判處死刑 , 如果被定罪了 , 我和我丈夫在公開場合發言 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些和透過人權團體 , 我們和許多其他受害者的家庭聚在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 她兒子被指控被指控 , 我心想: 「 真是個勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我想要和那位女士見面 , 我比較強壯 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我仍然深深的悲傷 ; 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我的兒子是受害者 , 我馬上得到同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她的兒子被指控了什麼 , 她沒有得到那樣的同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難和我一樣 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月見面 , 艾瑞克會告訴你這件事情是如何發生的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我請人權組織讓我接觸受害者的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	他們把我介紹給五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到了phyllis , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是這群人中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他都是兄弟姐妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我從她的眼睛看到她和我一樣 , 是個母親 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為一位母親 , 我經常受苦 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我14歲時結婚了 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 我十六歲時失去了第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	zacarias的故事實在太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然受苦 , 因為我兒子就像是被活埋了一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 。 我不知道他是否被折磨過 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他怎麼了 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 這麼一來 , 我的苦難對其他女性來說是很正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對於所有女性 , 所有賦予生命的母親 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	取決於我們女人 , 因為我們是女人 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們必須要親手合作 , 一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是反對女性 , 而是為我們、為我們女性、為我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我談的是對抗暴力、對抗恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校跟年輕的穆斯林女孩說話 , 她們不接受和她們的意願結婚 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以如果我能拯救其中一位年輕女孩 , 避免她們和我一樣的結婚、受苦 , 嗯 , 這是好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我會站在你們面前 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說我從aicha學到了這麼多東西 , 從那天開始 , 我們第一次和其他家庭成員會面 , 那是一次非常私人的會議 , 因為那是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕當時國家的超級愛國主義--我們這些家庭成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都很緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼想見我們 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她開始緊張 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 為什麼我們要和她見面 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們想從彼此身上得到什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們知道彼此的名字之前 , 我們已經擁抱和哭泣了 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們圍成一個圈子 , 圍著支援 , 提供協助 , 來自這種和解的人 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha一開始 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是有罪還是無辜 , 但我想告訴你們 , 我對你們家人的遭遇感到多麼遺憾 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道苦難是什麼 , 我覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人應該被公平審判、被懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她以那種方式向我們伸出援手 , 我想說 , 那是一種破冰的過程 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的是 , 我們都訴說自己的故事 , 我們都以人類的身分連結在一起 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	在午餐後--大概是午餐後三小時--我們覺得好像彼此認識了一輩子 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的 , 是一位女士 , 不單是她在現在的處境下如此慷慨 , 和當時的狀況 , 以及她兒子所做的事 , 還有她所擁有的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有見過這麼艱苦的生活 , 來自如此截然不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特殊的連結 , 我非常重視它 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我認為這一切都是為了害怕對方 , 但要踏出這一步 , 然後了解: 「 嘿 , 這不是那麼難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能和誰見面 , 我不知道 , 還是跟我很不一樣 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字來做結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	艾瑞克:我想說 , 我們得要試著認識其他人 , 另一位 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須要寬容 , 你的心也要寬容 , 你的心也要寬容 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定要包容 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有一天 , 我們都能和平共處 , 並尊重彼此 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這就是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界上太多人無法取得乾淨飲用水 。 工程師麥可普立查做了些改變 , 發明可攜式的生物安全濾鏡 , 讓水能在幾秒鐘內變成最可愛的飲用水 。 2009年的tedglobal示範 。

michael pritchard's water filter turns filthy water drinkable	麥可普立查的水過濾器轉變成了骯髒的飲用水 。
i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談談幾件事 。
the first thing is water .	第一件事是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都很享受這幾天在研討會提供給你們的水 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這是安全的來源 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是這樣呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是來自這樣的一個源頭呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	接著 , 統計數字會顯示 , 你們之中有一半的人會受痢疾所苦 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	我過去談過很多關於統計和提供安全飲用水的條件 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但它們似乎無法通過 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經想出為什麼了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	因為 , 用當前的思考 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法去思考解決問題 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們就關掉:我們、政府和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想告訴各位 , 透過不同的思考方式 , 問題已經被解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 從我開始演講到現在 , 全世界還有一萬三千人患有痢疾 。
and four children have just died .	四個孩子剛剛死了 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶 , 因為我很生氣 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們大多數一樣 , 正坐著 , 2004年聖誕節後的隔天 , 看著令人沮喪的消息 , 不斷在電視上播放 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的幾週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝下受污染的水 , 或面對死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	那真的讓我難以忘懷 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風襲擊了美國的一邊 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這裡是第一個世界國家 , 咱們來看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道要花五天才能把水送到超級穹頂嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上為電視機和水開槍 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時我決定要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	我花了很多時間在我的車庫裡 , 接下來的幾週 , 還有在我的廚房裡 , 讓我太太很沮喪 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 在幾次失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想出了這個 , lifesaver濾水瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好吧 , 現在來談談科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lissaver之前 , 最好的手工過濾器只能過濾200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	這絕對會穿過那200奈米的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	lisaver濾水孔是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 沒有任何東西能通過 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我來示範一下 。
would you like to see that ?	各位想看看嗎 ?
i spent all the time setting this up , so i guess i should .	我花了很多時間為此設定 , 所以我應該這樣做 。
we're in the fine city of oxford .	我們在美好的牛津城 。
so someone's done that up .	有人這樣做了 。
fine city of oxford , so what i've done is i've gone and got some water from the river cherwell , and the river thames , that flow through here . and this is the water .	美好的牛津城市 , 我所做的是從cherwell河取了一些水 , 而泰姆斯河 , 流過這裡 。 這就是水 。
but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我當時想 , 如果我們身在孟加拉的洪水區中 , 水不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	於是我拿了一些東西來加進去 。
and this is from my pond .	這是從我的池塘來的 。
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	聞一下吧 , 攝影師先生 。
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們就把它倒進去 。
michael pritchard: okay . we've got some runoff from a sewage plant farm .	michaelpritchard:好的 , 我們有一些廢水處理廠 。
so i'm just going to put that in there .	所以我就把它放進去 。
put that in there . there we go .	把它放進去 。 可以了 。
and some other bits and pieces , chuck that in there .	還有其他的零件和碎片 , 把它丟進去 。
and i've got a gift here from a friend of mine's rabbit .	我這裡有一份來自我朋友的兔子的禮物 。
so we're just going to put that in there as well .	我們也把它放進去 。
the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	lifesaver濾水瓶真的很簡單 。
you just scoop the water up .	你只要把水往上抽 。
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用一個水壺來展示給你們看 。 讓我們把那個糞便放進去 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	那還不夠髒 。 我們來稍微攪拌一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好 , 現在我要用這個非常骯髒的水 , 把它放在這裡 。 你還想喝杯酒嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好 , 開始了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些幫浦 。 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這就是必要之處 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我跳出這個茶 , 無菌的飲用水就會流出來 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	來了 。 注意電 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	那是安全的 , 無菌的飲用水 。
there you go chris .	來吧 , 克里斯
what's it taste of ?	它的味道是什麼 ?
let's see chris's program throughout the rest of the show . okay ?	我們來看看克里斯在節目的其他部分 。 好嗎 ?
okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好的 。 世界各地有數千人使用lifesaver濾水瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它能維持6 , 000公升 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它過期時 , 使用失敗保險技術 , 系統就會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把貨櫃拿出來 。 彈一個新貨櫃 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	另外還有六千公升是有用的 。
so let's look at the applications .	我們來看看這個應用程式 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	然後 , 幾個禮拜後 , 我們成立了營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫來到難民營 , 取得安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在一個難民營會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病會傳播開來 , 需要更多資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題會變成自我延續 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但透過不同的思考和運送這些資源 , 人們可以留在原地 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自行製造無菌飲用水 , 然後開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	這並不需要天然災害才行 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊思維、國家基礎建設和管道的成本實在太昂貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你計算機運算這些數字時 , 你就用完了 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這就是 「 思考不同 」 的位元 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水和使用人造程序來實現 , 讓我們用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 免費分解水 , 運送到那裡 , 把水倒到山上、河流和溪流中 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 靠近水源 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的就是讓它無菌 。 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	我們可以用lifesaver濾水瓶 。
or we could use one of these .	或者 , 我們可以用其中一種 。
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 用的是jerry罐子 。
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這將會處理兩萬五千公升的水 , 這足夠一個四個家庭 , 三年都能做到 。
and how much does it cost ?	它要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	每天跑大約半分錢 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 用不同的方式處理水 , 母親和孩子不再需要每天花四小時來取得水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	牠們可以從附近的來源取得 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	只要八十億美元 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目標 , 讓沒有安全飲用水的人數減半 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	為了說明這一點 , 英國政府每年花大約120億英鎊在國外援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停在這裡 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有了200億美元 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	結果是每年因此受苦的三十五億人 , 每年有兩百萬名孩童會活下來 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	廣大的阿什丹聲稱我們正處於歷史中 , 權力從未改變過的方式 。 在tedxbrussel的一場演說中 , 他排除了他所看到的三個重大的全球轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化 。
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyashdown:全球權力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩是一位非常有名的英國詩人在十九世紀末寫的 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	據說它在1930年代在邱吉爾的腦部迴盪 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩說: 「 夏天的小山上 , 躺在溪流的河流中 , 我聽到遙遠的鼓聲 , 像在夢中聽到的聲音 , 遙遠、近近近近、低音 , 在路上迴盪著 , 親愛的朋友和食物到粉末 , 士兵步行 , 很快就會死亡 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩有興趣的人 , 這首詩是 " a.housman " 寫的 " 購物小姐 " 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但 , 休斯曼所了解到的 , 你也在尼爾森交響曲中聽到的是19世紀漫長、熱天、銀夏天的穩定夏天即將接近 , 我們即將進入歷史上可怕的時期之一 , 當權力改變時 , 我們即將進入史上最可怕的時期之一 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	女士們先生們 , 這些時期總是伴隨著亂流 , 常常是血液 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我給你們的訊息是 , 我相信我們會被譴責 , 只活在歷史上的那些時刻 , 當那些已成立的秩序開始改變 , 新的世界觀 , 世界上的新勢力開始形成時 ,
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	這些是--我們今天清楚地看到了--幾乎總是非常混亂的時代 , 非常艱難的時代 , 甚至是非常血腥的時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順道一提 , 每一世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會爭辯說 , 上次發生時 , 休斯曼的感受到了 , 教堂的感受也是當權力從古老的國家 , 歐洲的舊勢力通過 , 橫跨大西洋 , 到美國的新興勢力--美國在本世紀初 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在過去一個世紀 , 歐洲的權力都被用在兩場血腥的災難中 , 第一部份和第二部份:兩場大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經稱他們為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是一種更精確的描述方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	女士們先生們 , 我們生活在其中一個時代 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天要談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	第一個是權力的轉變
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個面向 , 是我想要指出的 , 從來沒有像現在這樣發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談權力正在發生的轉變 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的事 , 在某種意義上 , 很可怕 , 因為從來沒有發生過這種事 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到希臘的權力移轉到羅馬 , 在歐洲文明中發生的權力移轉 , 但我們看到有些不太一樣的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	因為權力不只會從國家轉移到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今的情況是 , 負責任的權力 , 受到法律的牽制 , 在國家的制度裡 , 現在已經在非常大量的全球舞台上移民了 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力 , 我們談到全球化市場 , 但事實上 , 它是全球化的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	而在國家的層面上 , 負責任的權力會受到法律的影響 , 在國際舞台上沒有 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球權力掌握在哪裡:網際網路的力量 , 衛星廣播的力量 , 貨幣改變大筆貨幣的力量 , 現在流通了32倍的貨幣交易所需的金錢 , 應該要在那裡資助改變金的變革者 , 若你願意 , 金融的推論者 , 最近才把我們帶到膝蓋的金融商業推動力 , 比發展中國家還要強大32倍 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些人生活在一個全球化的空間 , 幾乎沒有受到規範 , 沒有受到法律規範 , 人們可能不受約束 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在這套潛水服就是強大的動作
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	在沒有限制的情況下 , 使用最有權力的人總是適合的 , 但歷史教訓是 , 遲早 , 不受法律規範的空間受到侵害 , 不僅僅是你想要國際貿易、網路等等 , 還有你不想要國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義的東西 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911的揭示是 , 即使你是世界上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 住在那空間的人 , 可以攻擊你 , 即使是在九月的一個早晨 , 都能攻擊你 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 四百萬美金中大約有60%被用來資助9/11的金額 , 其實是通過雙子星大樓的機構9/11摧毀的機構 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	要知道 , 我們的敵人也用了這個空間──大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播──來繞過它們的毒害 , 重點是要摧毀我們的系統和方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	不論遲早 , 歷史的規則就是權力要掌控的地方 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	因此 , 如同我相信的 , 如果我們這個時代的一個現象是全球化的權力 , 那麼我們這個時代的挑戰之一就是將統治者帶到國際空間 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 在未來的數十年 , 將來我們將能夠達到那樣的目標:將治理帶到國際舞台 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在談政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說建立一些全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順道一提 , 我自己的觀點是 , 女士們先生們 , 聯合國和機構不太可能實現 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	國際行動需要一個方法來合法化 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當談到管理全球空間時 , 我猜 , 透過更多聯合國機構的創立 , 這種事並不會發生 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	事實上 , 強權人士聚在一起 , 建立以條約為基礎的系統、以條約為基礎的協議 , 來管理這個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你去看 , 你可以看到他們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:合約的以條約為基礎的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎的組織 , 然而 , 強大到足以支撐最強大的國家 , 即便是美國 , 也要考量必要條約 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都議定書:努力打造一個以條約為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國集團現在 , 我們知道我們必須組成一個機構 , 它能夠將政府帶到金融空間 , 做為財務猜測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是二十國集團的目標 , 一個合約為基礎的機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有個問題 , 我們等一下會回到這個問題上 , 如果你把最強大的組織結合起來 , 在合約的制度下 , 填滿管理空間 , 那麼那些被遺漏的弱者會怎麼樣 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們馬上就會回到這個問題上 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個信息是 , 如果你在亂度過這些混亂的時間時 , 或多或少是亂度 , 那麼我們的成功 , 會大大地取決於我們帶合理的管理到全球空間的能力 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著這一切開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和像這樣的觀眾談談這件事 , 但權力不僅僅是垂直的轉變 , 也是橫向的轉變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會說 , 文明的歷史 , 一直都是文明聚集在海洋上 , 最早出現在地中海的文明 , 近期在西大西洋的後代 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	對我來說 , 我們現在看到的是一個基本的權力轉移 , 廣義來說 , 遠離大西洋棋周圍的國家 , 轉移到太平洋岸邊的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這一切都是從經濟力量開始的 , 但它總是這樣開始的 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的增強 , 發生在世界上其他正在成長的權力 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我想事實上 , 這不是從西方移轉到東方 , 有些不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我猜 , 值得一提的是 , 美國在接下來的十年、十五年 , 仍然是地球上最強大的國家 , 但她掌握權力的情境現在已經徹底改變了 , 它已經徹底地改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們正要走過五十年 , 最不尋常的時代 , 在這個世界中 , 我們有一個完全獨立的世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每一個指南針或反對的指南都必須被指引到華盛頓的位置 , 一個巨人的世界 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但在歷史上這不是常見的情況 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在所發生的是更正常的歷史 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到多極化的世界出現了 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	目前為止 , 美國一直是世界的主要特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保留最強大的國家 , 但他們將會是世上最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你會開始看到其他的權力建設在中國 , 當然 , 我自己的猜測是 , 中國要成為偉大並不是平順的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	會很糟糕 , 因為中國在自由經濟後開始將她的社會給民主化 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是另一個主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度 , 巴西 。
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 世界看起來越來越像十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	歐洲在19世紀 , 一個偉大的英國外交部長 , 坎寧 , 曾經形容它為 「 歐洲權力協會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡 , 一個五面的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是扮演著平衡 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林合作 , 英國和維也納和羅馬合作 , 來提供平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在一個由獨立世界主導的時期 , 你有固定的聯盟──北約組織 , 華沙聯盟協議 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定的兩極性就意味著結盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但 , 多種權力的兩極性就意味著要轉變和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們正在進入的世界 , 我們越來越會看到我們的盟友不是固定的 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	偉大的英國外交部長坎寧曾說過: 「 英國有共同的興趣 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會越來越常看到 , 即使我們身處西方 , 也要向外伸出援手 , 超越大西洋的舒適圈 , 和其他人聯盟 , 若我們想在世界上做事的話 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	值得注意的是 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方國家還不夠好 ; 我們必須讓其他人加入 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	在這個例子中 , 我們必須引進阿拉伯聯盟
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我猜 , 伊拉克和阿富汗是最後一次西方試圖自行做這件事 , 而我們還沒有成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我猜我們已經達到400年的終點了我說400年因為這是歐特曼帝國的終點西方強權、西方制度和西方價值觀的終點
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道嗎 , 到目前為止 , 如果西方國家能團結起來 , 它能在世界上的每個角落提出和丟棄 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是真的了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以上次世界大戰之後的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家聚集了布雷頓森林機構 , 世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金會--問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須打電話給其他人 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為你做一個預測 , 這可能更令人吃驚 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們已經達到400年的終點了 , 那時西方的力量已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國絕對不會介入到世界各地的調停和平 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	哦 , 好嗎 ? 為什麼不 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷特下服役 , 在藍色旗幟下服役 , 在聯合國的指令下服役 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11個人 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	要解決索馬利海盜最大的海軍內容是什麼 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍陸戰隊
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是一流的慈善家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要維持航道的開放 。
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和那些我們不共享價值觀的人做生意 , 但 , 目前 , 我們共有共同利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一個全新的角度來看這個正在興起的世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素 , 完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天 , 在我們的現代世界中 , 由於網路 , 由於人們在這裡所談論的事物 , 每件事都和每件事連結在一起 。
we are now interdependent .	我們是互相依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在相互關聯 , 作為國家 , 個人 , 以一種從來沒有這樣過 , 從來沒有如此過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國與國之間的關係總是存在的 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交是管理國家的相互關係 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們緊密地被鎖在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥得到豬流感 , 24小時後 , 查爾斯德高樂機場出現了問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟倒下了 , 大量的崩潰 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯大草原上有火 , 非洲的食物暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深地、深深地相互關聯 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家獨立行動 , 而不是與他人建立關係 , 不再與他人合作 , 不再是個可行的主張 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為國家的行動不是只侷限於自己 , 也不足以讓國家控制自己的領土 , 因為國外的影響現在開始影響到國內發生的事 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我當時是英國最後一次帝國戰爭的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國家的防禦是一回事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的海軍有多強 , 我們的盟友有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	敵人就在城牆外 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人就在城牆內 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想要談談我的國家的辯護 , 我必須和衛生部長談談 , 因為流行病對我的健康造成威脅 , 我必須和農業部談談 , 因為糧食安全對我的安全造成威脅 , 我必須和產業部談談談 , 因為當我們從網路戰爭中看到我們的敵人 , 我們的攻擊現正是攻擊我們的敵人 , 我必須和當地的安全局談談 , 因為在我們的城市中 , 在我們的城市中 , 77/7 , 都在我們的家中發生了什麼事 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	不再是這樣 , 國家的安全只是士兵和國防部的問題 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它的能力是鎖定它的機構 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴我們一件非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴我們 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直架構 , 建立在工業革命的經濟模式 , 垂直階級制度 , 專門化工作任務 , 指揮結構完全錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	各位在商業界都知道 , 我們這個時代的典範結構 , 各位先生女士 , 就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	重要的是你有能力建立起重要網絡 , 不論在你的政府內部或外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是ashdown的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 別問我ashdown的第一條法則和第二條法則 , 因為我還沒發明出來 , 如果第三條法則總是比較好聽 , 對吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	第三條法則是 , 在現代社會 , 每件事都連結在一起 , 最重要的是 , 你能做什麼 , 就是你能和別人做什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的是 , 不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊團體 , 不論你是商業活動點 , 你的中間人際關係 , 你和他人建立關係的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	在工業界 , 政府不懂 。
but now one final thing .	但 , 最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是的話 , 女士們先生們--我們現在是以前所未見的方式聯繫在一起的 , 那也是我們和彼此有著共同的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 也是第一次 , 集體防禦 , 主宰我們國家安全的概念已經不夠了了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	過去 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更有權力 , 我就安全了 , 如果我的國家比他們的國家更有權力 , 我就安全了 ; 我的盟國 , 像北約組織 , 比他們的盟友更有權力 , 我就安全了 。
it is no longer the case .	情況不再是如此了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的興起 , 意味著 , 漸漸地 , 我和我的敵人有著同樣的命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交官的時候 , 在1970年代與蘇聯在日內瓦與蘇聯的裁決協定談判時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們知道我們有共同的命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平來到北愛爾蘭因為兩方都意識到零和遊戲是行不通的
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人有著共同的命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	在中東和平最大的阻礙之一是以色列和巴勒斯坦人都不明白他們有共同的命運
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 突然間 , 各位先生女士 , 隨年齡增長有遠見的詩人和詩人的提議 , 變成了我們必須認真看待的公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我先從一首詩開始 , 先以一首詩作結 。
the great poem of john donne's .	多恩的偉大詩作
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 別因為鈴聲響起 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是孤島 」 。
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	這句話是這樣的: 「 每個人的死亡都影響著我 , 因為我也參與其中 , 派遣我去問鐘聲為誰響 , 鈴聲為我響 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對約翰多恩來說 , 這是道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 算是我們生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽生活和健康的道路 , 丹•巴特納和團隊研究世界的 「 藍色區域 」 , 這些社區的老年人和vim和活力一起生活 , 為了記錄年齡 。 在tedxtc , 他共有9個常見的飲食習慣和生活習慣 , 讓他們能在一百歲以上流逝 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索食物、健康、生命、科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活到100+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	丹麥雙胞胎研究指出 , 在某些生物限制下 , 平均人壽命只有百分之十是由我們的基因所決定 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其他百分之九十是由我們的生活方式決定 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍寶地的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能找出一個長壽的實證公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 長壽的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們大概不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南海灘減肥 , 或阿特金斯減肥法 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國農業部食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們什麼 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲博士告訴我們 ,
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 許多困惑都讓我們真正活得更久了 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到補給品時 , 你該拿嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	荷爾蒙或復原劑呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的有在其中嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神層面呢 ? 我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們尋找長壽的方法是與國家地理和國家老化研究所合作 , 找到四個人口統計的確認區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 請一組專家來做法性地檢查這些人的所作所為 , 來提煉跨文化的精華 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	到最後 , 我要告訴各位 , 這種精華是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想要揭露一些常見的迷思 , 關於長壽的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是如果你真的努力嘗試過活到100歲
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 在美國 , 只有五千人中的一個活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	雖然這是美國成長最快的人口 , 很難達到一百歲 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是我們沒有長壽的規劃 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被設計為一種叫做 「 繁衍成功 」 的東西 。
i love that word .	我很愛這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起了大學日 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 成功 」 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一個世代 , 你的孩子有孩子的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那之後 , 演化的效應完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類動物 , 如果你是老鼠或大象 , 或人類 , 在兩者之間 , 都是一樣的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	若要活到一百歲 , 你不只得要有很棒的生活方式 , 你還得要贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有些治療方法可以幫助緩慢、逆轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	仔細想想 , 我們有99件事情可以老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要你的腦袋缺氧幾分鐘 , 這些腦細胞就會死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	打網球太難 , 膝蓋上 , 把軟骨弄壞 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈會堵塞 。 我們的大腦會用斑塊固定起來 , 然後我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情會出錯 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 和t萬億個 「 t 」 有關 , 我們在這裡談的是國家債務的數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年就會轉一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們翻過來 , 就會造成一些傷害 , 造成傷害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它以指數成長 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像我們都有披頭四或老鷹專輯的日子 , 我們會複製一份錄製在錄音帶上 , 讓我們的朋友複製錄錄音帶 , 很快地 , 一代又一代的錄音帶聽起來像垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化的速度比一個12歲的人快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有辦法減緩老化或停止老化 , 我在這裡幹嘛 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人類身體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約九十年 , 多一點是女性 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但美國的預期壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	接下來的某處 , 我們會在桌子上留下十二年美好的年齡 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年是我們能得到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 這些年大部分都不需要慢性病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要消失這些年的最佳方法就是看看世界各地的文化 , 實際體驗到它們的文化 , 人們活到一百歲的比例比我們高出十倍 , 預期壽命是十幾年 , 中年死亡率是這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現第一個藍色區域距離義大利海岸大約125英哩 , 位在薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島 , 整個島嶼大約有一百四十萬人 , 但只有在高地 , 一個叫做努羅省的地方 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡是男性最長壽的地區 , 比美國這裡多出十倍的百歲人瑞 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	在這個地方 , 人們不只活到一百歲 , 他們還帶著不凡的活力 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	一百零二歲的老人還騎自行車去上班 , 砍柴 , 還能打敗比他們年輕六十年的老人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上會回到基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它實際上是一個孤立的青銅時代文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地非常缺乏土地 , 它們大多是牧羊人 , 有時是定期、低強度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要以植物為主 , 以能帶到田野的食物為主 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種尚未發酵的全麥麵包 , 叫做全麥麵包 , 用一種來自全麥做的乳酪 , 一種來自青草餵養的動物 , 乳酪含在omega-3脂肪酸 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自玉米餵養的動物 , 還有一種葡萄酒 , 比世界上任何酒都多三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一就是他們對待老年人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會公平似乎在24歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 你越年長 , 你就越有公平 , 你就越有智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 不是看到運動畫的泳裝日曆 , 而是百歲人瑞月曆 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這不只對你老化的父母保持親近家庭的好處 , 還包含了預期壽命四到六年的研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩子也有好處 , 他們的死亡率較低 , 疾病的比率也比較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一邊找到第二個藍色區域 , 位於南方的東南方 , 約800英里 , 位在俄亥俄州的阿基拉瓦島 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在大島的北部 , 這是世界長壽的原點 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這裡是最老的雌性居住地 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這裡的人有世界上最長的無障礙預期壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活得很久 , 通常在睡眠中死亡 , 很快 , 常常 , 我可以告訴你 , 經過性行為之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人多活七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	在美國 , 百歲人瑞的比例是五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	五分之一是結腸癌和乳癌的比率 , 美國的大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的比例是六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	而事實是 , 這種文化產生了這些數字 , 強烈表示他們有東西要教我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	同樣的 , 以植物為主的飲食 , 裡面滿是蔬菜 , 裡面有許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們的飲食量是美國人的8倍 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比起吃什麼 , 更重要的是他們如何吃它 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略來避免過食 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:它們吃的盤子比較小 , 所以每次坐著都會少吃一點卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其提供家庭風格 , 不如你說話 , 可以無意識地吃東西 , 他們在櫃檯上供應食物 , 把食物帶走 , 然後帶到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一句三千歲的格言我認為這是有史以來最偉大的飲食建議
it was invented by confucius .	它是由孔子所發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食就是所謂的 「 哈拉 」 、 「 辣 」 、 「 辣 」 飲食 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在吃飯前會先說 , 提醒他們 , 吃到80%的肚子就不吃了 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	足夠的感覺要花半小時才能從肚子傳到腦袋 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住要在80%時停下來 , 這樣就能幫助你不去做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 和薩丁尼亞一樣 , okinawa有少數的社會結構 , 我們可以用長壽來連結 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會致命 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國人平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在只剩下1.5% 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你幸運地出生在俄亥俄州 , 你出生在一個系統中 , 你自動有五十個朋友 , 和他們一起度過人生 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為 「 模合 」 。 如果你在模合裡 , 如果你幸運的話 , 你會被期望分享 「 反彈 」 。 如果情況不好 , 孩子生病、父母過世 , 總是有人在背後支持你 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這五位女士 , 這五位女士 , 已經在一起九十七年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人生活分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作是有生產力的
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 砰 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這意味著要退休給簡單的椅子 , 或是去亞利桑那州打高爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語中甚至沒有退休詞 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 有一個詞貫穿了你的整個人生 , 這個詞是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	粗略來說 , 意思是 「 你早上起床的理由 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位一百零二歲的凱特大師而言 , 他的ikigai帶著這件武術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位一百歲的漁夫來說 , 每週捕魚三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究所真的給了我們一個問卷 , 給予這些百歲人瑞 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們非常的文化天分 , 那些提出問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位一百零二歲的老太太來說 , 她的生存還是她的曾曾曾曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩在101歲半前被分開 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她感覺如何抱著曾曾曾曾曾孫女 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭放回去 , 說: 「 感覺就像跳上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理雜誌的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍寶地 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子我們研究明尼蘇達的草原那裡百歲人瑞的比例非常高
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長壽的人口 , 其中有七天的新興醫師集中在加州的羅馬林達市 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	基督復臨派是保守的方法論者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們從星期五日落到星期六日落的日落慶祝安息日 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 二十四小時的庇護 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	相較之下 , 他們遵循五個小習慣 , 傳達給他們非凡的長壽 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性平均壽命是八十歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對於一位新進主義的女性來說 , 他們的預期壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差異更明顯 , 他們預期比美國人多活了11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林的研究 。 我認為它完全描述了這個藍寶地計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異質的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	白色、黑色、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點是一套非常小的生活習慣他們一生中大部分時間都遵循著儀式
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中獲取飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	創世紀:第一章 , 第二十九章 , 上帝談到豆子和種子 , 再談另一章 , 談到綠色植物 , 很明顯少了肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這個庇護所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不管多忙 , 工作壓力多大 , 孩子需要被驅使 , 停止一切 , 專注在他們的神 , 他們的社交網路上 , 然後 , 在宗教裡 , 基本上就在走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	強大之處不在於它偶爾會發生 , 權力是它一生中每週都在發生 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不難 。 一點都不花錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	基督復臨派的讀者也傾向和其他的讀者相處 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個基督復臨派對 , 你不會看到人們在游泳jimbeam或滾動一個聯合體 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	取而代之的是 , 他們在談論下一次的自然步行 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們以深刻、可測量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這種文化已經產生了埃爾斯沃•華倫 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	ellsworthwhareham97歲
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是百萬富翁 , 但當包商想要花六千美金來建立一個隱私圍籬時 , 他說: 「 為了這一類的錢 , 我自己去做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	接下來的三天 , 他出去挖水泥 , 到處拖著poles 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預料的是 , 或許在第四天他到了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是桌上的那個人 , 而是做開心手術的人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲的他仍然每個月做二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 103歲 , 一個活躍的牛仔 , 早上開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡穿上板子 , 把公雞尾巴丟出去 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子真的住在這兩個城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她每天一開始就有舉重 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她在她的根部上染上了1994年的卡迪拉克賽維爾 , 在聖貝納迪納迪諾高速公路上撕下了淚水 , 在那裡她仍然是七個不同組織的志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾經參加過19次硬體考察 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是你見過唯一一個騎腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠的人 , 沒有防曬霜 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有任何冒險比和瑪格頓騎車的機會更恐怖 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三種文化中有什麼共同點 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都在做些什麼呢 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功地歸結為九種 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自從此以來 , 我們已經完成了兩個藍寶地的探險 , 這些共同的探險家也成立了 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一個 , 我即將要強調一個狂熱 , 沒有一個運動 , 至少我們對運動的看法 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之的是 , 他們建立自己的生活 , 使他們不斷地被推入實體活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球女人站在地上下 , 她們每天坐在地上三十或四十次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直房子裡 , 樓梯上下 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店、教堂 , 或去朋友家裡都要走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有便利 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕可以做院子工作或做家事 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	跑步機燃燒的熱量和跑步機一樣 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做意圖性的身體活動 , 他們會享受的東西 , 他們會走路 , 唯一證明的認知衰退 , 他們都會有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式生活 , 所以他們有正確的人生觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間來降低 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 第七天的新教徒祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人有祖先的復仇 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你趕時間或壓力大時 , 會引發發發炎反應 , 這反應和阿茲海默症和心血管疾病相關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天放慢15分鐘 , 你就會把那發炎狀態變成更加反炎狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們用詞彙來表達目的、生存的、生存的、像是okinawans的意思 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 和退休那一年 。
