your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能會感覺像朋友 , 但真朋友會給你一杯微笑 。 在ted2013年 , 凱勒•瑞納多示範romo , 智慧型手機驅動你的迷你機器人 , 可以在路上和你一起走路 , 滑動一杯咖啡 , 跨過桌子 , 和你做出可編程表達的反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個迷你機器人 , 由你的手機供電 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	請舉手 , 有多少人家裡有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	你們不多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好 , 請舉手 , 如果你不包含roomba在家裡有多少機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這是我們在romotive公司試圖解決的問題 , 我和romotive另外二十位宅友正著迷於解決這個問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的很想製造一個人都可以使用的機器人 , 不管你是八或八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是個非常困難的問題 , 因為你得要做出一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 這不僅是真的負擔得起 , 而且它必須要是人們真的想要帶回家 , 帶著孩子們到處走 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不能很詭異或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該要友善、可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個機器人 , 用你已經知道且很愛你的iphone來當作他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	透過iphone處理器的力量 , 我們可以創造一個可以無線上網的機器人 , 且電腦的視覺能力是150美元 , 這大約是過去機器人所花費的1% 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他正處於生物模式 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	他其實是用這個裝置上的攝影機來跟著我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我躲開 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很謹慎 , 所以他會一直盯著我 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我過來這裡 , 他會轉身跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我走到這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會像其他生物一樣害怕 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以在很多方面 , romo就像一隻有自己想法的寵物一樣 。
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探索世界--喔哦 , romo累了--如果我想要用romo來探索世界 , 我其實可以把他和任何ios設備連結起來 。
so here's the ipad .	這是ipad 。
and romo will actually stream video to this device .	romo會將視訊串流到這個裝置上 。
so i can see everything that romo sees , and i get a robot'seyeview of the world .	我能看到romo所看到的一切 , 我得到機器人的視角世界 。
now this is a free app on the app store , so if any of you guys had this app on your phones , we could literally right now share control of the robot and play games together .	這是appstore的免費應用程式 , 如果你們任何人在手機上有這個應用程式 , 我們現在就可以分享機器人的控制權 , 一起玩遊戲 。
so i'll show you really quickly , romo actually he's streaming video , so you can see me and the entire ted audience .	我會很快的給你們看 , romo實際上是在串流影片 , 所以你可以看到我和整個ted觀眾 。
if i get in front of romo here .	如果我在romo面前的話 。
and if i want to control him , i can just drive .	如果我想要控制他 , 我就可以開車 。
so i can drive him around , and i can take pictures of you .	所以我可以帶他到處走 , 我可以幫你拍照 。
i've always wanted a picture of a 1 , 500person ted audience .	我一直都想要有一張一千五百位ted觀眾的照片 。
so i'll snap a picture .	所以我拍了一張照片 。
and in the same way that you scroll through content on an ipad , i can actually adjust the angle of the camera on the device .	就像你在ipad上滑動內容一樣 , 我其實可以調整裝置上攝影機的角度 。
so there are all of you through romo's eyes .	透過romo的眼睛 , 你們所有人都能看見 。
and finally , because romo is an extension of me , i can express myself through his emotions .	最後 , 因為romo是我的延伸 , 我可以透過他的情緒表達我自己 。
so i can go in and i can say let's make romo excited .	所以我可以進去 , 說讓我們讓romo興奮一點 。
but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但關於romo , 最重要的是 , 我們想要創造出完全直覺的東西 。
you do not have to teach someone how to drive romo .	你不需要教別人如何駕駛romo 。
in fact , who would like to drive a robot ?	事實上 , 誰會想開機器人呢 ?
thank you , scott .	謝謝你 , 史考特 。
and even cooler , you actually don't have to be in the same geographic location as the robot to control him .	更酷的是 , 你其實不需要和機器人在同一個地理位置來控制他 。
so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上是在任何兩個智慧型設備之間串流雙向的聲音和影片 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	你可以透過瀏覽器登入 , 有點像在輪子上的skype 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	我們剛剛談到遠端臨場 , 這是一個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲的女孩 , 例如 , 她有一支iphone , 她媽媽會給她買機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 放在機器人上 , 發送電子郵件給住在該國的另一邊的祖母 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	祖母可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩捉迷藏 , 每天晚上十五分鐘 , 否則她只能一次或兩次看見她孫女 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是romo今天能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我想談談我們未來正在努力的事來結束我的演講 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這是我們的一位工程師 , dom , 在週末建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在谷歌開放框架上 , 叫做blockly 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這樣你就可以拖著這些程式碼 , 放下這些程式碼 , 創造出任何你想要的機器人行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何寫romo的行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你可以在瀏覽器中模擬這些行為 , 也就是你在左邊看到romo在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載到你的機器人上 , 在現實生活中執行這個程式 , 在現實生活中執行 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有你引以為傲的東西 , 你可以和世界上每個擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些有wi-fi功能的機器人都能互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們如此專注於建造一個人人都能訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為個人機器人中最有說服力的使用方式是個人化的 。
they change from person to person .	它們會從人變成人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以我們認為 , 如果你要在家裡裝一個機器人 , 那機器人應該是你自己的想像力的表現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	我希望我能告訴你們個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道的是 , 它不是10年或100億美金 , 也不是一個大型的人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它取決於像你們一樣的小型敏捷機器人 , 以及像你們這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及要讓你們所有機器人 , 我們等不及要看看你們建造了什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和活動家伊莎貝爾•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 也在這場演說中 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女人、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德訴說著熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你 。 能來到這裡是最聰明的人之一 , 真的很可怕 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴各位幾個關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	猶太人說我很喜歡 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	比真相更真實的是什麼 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是說故事的人 。 我想要傳達比事實更真實的東西 , 不是關於我們共同的人性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都吸引我 , 有些則令我困擾 , 直到最後我寫下它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我知道我們身邊的謎團 , 所以我寫了巧合、預兆、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我一直活在匿名中 , 直到2006年2月 , 我帶著奧林匹克旗在義大利的冬季奧運 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成了名人 。 現在大家認得我是梅西百貨 。 我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我告訴你們我四分鐘的名氣 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	其中一個籌辦奧運的籌辦人打電話告訴我 , 我被選為旗手之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答說 , 這肯定是誤認的案例 , 因為身為運動員 , 我完全是你能從運動員那邊得到的 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定我能走在體育館裡 , 不用路人 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運國旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性 , 代表五大洲 , 和三位奧運金牌得主 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說 , 穿著制服 , 要求我的測量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我有個幻想 , 在一個鬆軟的主動脈下 , 看起來像一個米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我在杜林 , 在那裡 , 充滿熱情的群眾歡呼 , 當時街上有八十個奧運團隊都在 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	這些運動員犧牲了所有的競爭 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得獲得勝利 , 但運氣的元素是 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一小塊雪 , 一英吋的冰 , 一股風力 , 可以決定種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 除了訓練或運氣之外 , 最重要的是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才能得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	一切都和熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	杜林街上滿是紅色海報 , 宣佈奧運的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就在這裡 , 不是一直都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們決定我們的命運的原因 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中角色需要的:熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要長城長、異議人士、冒險家、局外人和叛軍 , 他們會問問題、彎曲規則 , 並冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有 「 常識 」 的好人並不會做有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	它們只會製造好的前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了其他護旗手:三位運動員 , 以及女演員蘇珊莎蘭登和蘇菲雅羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	此外 , 有兩位有熱情的女性:旺加里•馬塔伊 , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種植了三千萬棵樹 。 透過這麼做 , 她改變了土壤、天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然也改變了許多村落的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	索馬利夫人 , 柬埔寨活躍人士 , 積極對抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣給妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男性強暴 , 他們相信和非常年輕的處女做愛 , 會治癒她們免於愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	有些妓院孩子被迫要每天接到5、15個客戶 , 如果他們反抗 , 他們就會被電擊折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡 , 我收到制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的那種服裝 , 但它離我預期的米其林人裝還很遠 。 其實不錯 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	除了蘇菲雅羅蘭 , 大部分的旗幟也都一樣 , 是美麗和熱情的普遍象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅七十多歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感、很薄、很高 , 有很深的皮膚 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你怎麼會有深色的皮膚 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當電視訪談中問到: 「 她怎麼能看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是直的 , 而我不會發出老人的聲音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	這裡有一些來自地球上最美麗的女性的免費建議 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有磨練 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有呼吸 , 沒有跟自己說話 , 沒有磨練 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	她並沒有說得那麼清楚 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在大約午夜的時候 , 我們被召喚到體育場的翅膀 , 擴音器發佈了奧林匹克旗 , 順便一提 , 音樂是從這裡開始的 , 艾達遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她比我高一呎 , 不算頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走路 , 像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿 , 把旗子放在肩膀上 。 我跑在我的尖端 , 手臂上拿著國旗 , 這樣我的頭其實是在該死的旗子下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的相機都是在蘇菲雅 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中 , 我也出現了 , 雖然常常出現在蘇菲雅的雙腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大多數男人都想去的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘就是奧林匹克體育館 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我先生雖然我對他解釋說 , 我們在私下所做的事通常會花不到四分鐘 , 但他不應該親自接受 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我對這四分鐘的報導都很精彩 , 因為我不想忘記 , 老年時摧毀了我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著奧運熱情的關鍵詞 。
so here's a tale of passion .	以下是關於熱情的故事
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	時間是1998年 , 地點是在剛果的圖西難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的人都是女人和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	在剛果 , 我們可以稱這個地方為死亡集中營 , 因為沒有被殺害的人 , 會因為疾病或飢餓而死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 羅絲•瑪班多和她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了 , 寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵強迫她看著她的丈夫被虐待和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她成功讓七個孩子活了下來 , 幾個月後 , 她生下了早產兒雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子割斷臍帶 , 用頭髮綁上它 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她用營地指揮官的名字來命名雙胞胎 , 讓雙胞胎得利 , 並用黑色茶餵食牠們 , 因為她的母乳無法維持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵衝進她的牢房強暴她大女兒時 , 她抓住她並拒絕放手 , 即使他們頭上拿著槍 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 這個家庭存活了16個月 , 然後 , 幸運地 , 還有一位年輕美國人沙夏•查諾夫的熱心人士 , 她成功地把她送上美國救援機 , 羅絲•瑪德歐和她的九個孩子 , 最後到了亞利桑那州的鳳凰城 , 在那裡生活和茁壯成長 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	瑪班多在斯瓦希里語意謂著偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角是堅強且充滿熱情的女性 , 像是蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不編造它們 , 不需要它 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都看得到 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在為女性、為女性工作 。
i know them well .	我對他們很熟悉 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古代 , 在世界末日 , 在父權的天主教和保守的家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪我五歲時是個憤怒的女權主義者 , 雖然這個詞還沒到達智利 , 所以沒有人知道我到底怎麼了 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就發現 , 要付出很高的代價來支付我的自由 , 還要向父權社會提出質疑 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付出代價 , 因為每當我得到的一擊 , 我都能提供兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒寶拉二十多歲時 , 她對我說 , 女權主義已經過時了 , 我應該繼續下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們打了一場記憶深刻的仗 。 女權主義已經過時了嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	沒錯 , 對於我女兒及今天在座各位一樣有特權的女性 , 但對世界上大部分的姊妹來說 , 她們仍然被迫結婚、賣淫、強迫工作她們有不想要的孩子 , 或無法餵飽的孩子 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或人生 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、毆打 , 有時甚至遭到懲罰 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對於現今大部分的西方年輕女性來說 , 被稱為女性主義者是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有性感過 , 但讓我保證我從來沒有停止調情 , 我很少受到男性的苦難 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義還沒死 , 絕對沒有 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 改變它 , 為了女神的緣故 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為 「 愛芙若蒂 」 , 或 「 金星 」 , 或 「 金星 」 , 或其他任何你想的 ; 名字無所謂 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就會支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這裡有另一個關於熱情的故事 , 一個令人難過的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這地方是孟加拉一個村莊的婦女診所 。
the year is 2005 .	時間是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫 , 她在三週的假期中擔任志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她已經準備好要清潔牙齒了 , 但當她到達那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生、沒有牙醫 , 而診所只是一間蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一排女子等了好幾個小時來接受治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人痛苦得很痛 , 因為她有數個壞掉的臼齒 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮知道唯一的解決方案就是拔掉不好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有被授權 , 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她常常冒險 , 她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶來了一些麻醉藥 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有顆勇敢且熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她鼓起了一名禱告 , 繼續前進營運 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病人鬆了一口氣 , 親了她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生專家又拔了更多牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人在等她丈夫 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	那位女士的臉看起來像個浮標 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫脹到連眼睛都看不見 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫、憤怒、威脅要殺掉美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到害怕 , 接著 , 翻譯說明病人的狀況和手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打了她 , 因為她不在家裡準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性是這樣生活的 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最窮的窮人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然世界上有三分之二的女性勞動力 , 但她們卻擁有不到世界百分之一的資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水低於男性 , 如果他們有薪水的話 , 他們會維持弱勢 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 且他們會不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實是 , 給予女性教育、工作、控制自己收入的能力、繼承和自己的財產 , 讓社會受益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果女性有能力 , 她的孩子和家人就會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家人能繁榮 , 村落就會繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家也一樣 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai去了肯亞的一個村莊 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和女人談 , 並解釋土地是貧瘠的 , 因為土地被砍伐和賣掉了樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女們種植新的樹木 , 用水澆灌 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	五、六年後 , 牠們有森林 , 土壤富含土壤 , 拯救了村落 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮、最倒退的社會總是會讓女性失望 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而 , 這種顯而易見的事實卻被政府以及慈善事業忽略了 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	女性專案的每一塊錢 , 每捐二十塊錢給男性專案計畫 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔人類的51% 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦權會改變一切 , 不只是科技、設計、娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性一起工作 , 連結、有知識、受教育的女性 , 能為這波波浪潮的星球帶來和平和繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	今天的任何戰爭中 , 死傷大部分都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 她們是附帶的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人跑遍世界 , 看看我們這一團糟 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大多數人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們希望一個保存生命的世界 , 生活品質也能給每個人充實 , 不只是為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月份 , 我看到費南多•博特羅在柏克萊大學圖書館的畫展 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有博物館或畫廊除了紐約畫廊裡的伯特羅的作品她敢展現這些畫作因為主題是阿布格萊布監獄
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	這些畫作包括酷刑和權力濫用 , 以大量的巴特羅風格呈現 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法從我的心中或我的心中得到那些影像 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是無辜的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 並迫使其他成員接受現實並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則隨時都在改變 , 但總是對它們有益 , 在這個例子中 , 下滲效應 , 在經濟上行不通的效應 , 效果完美 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待從梯子的上方滑到下方 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和小孩 , 尤其是窮人 , 都在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最貧窮的男人也有可能會虐待女人或小孩的人 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我受夠了少數人透過性別、收入、種族和階級的能力 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 該是成熟的時候了 , 在我們的文明中做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但真正的改變 , 我們需要女性能量來管理這個世界 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要相當多有權力的女性 , 我們需要培養男性的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	當然 , 我指的是年輕男性 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老年人是絕望的 ; 我們必須等他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很希望蘇菲雅羅倫的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若要選擇 , 我寧願有顆勇敢的心臟 , 包羅斯瑪利•瑪塔伊、索瑪利媽、珍妮和蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得更美好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是讓它更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 這是有可能的 。 看看這個房間裡的所有知識、精力、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們擺脫風扇 , 捲起袖子 , 激情地工作 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦這麼大的城市裡 , 有三千萬份餐是服務過的 。 但所有食物從哪裡來的 ? 建築師卡洛琳鋼鐵討論了餵養城市的每日奇蹟 , 並展現出古老的食物路線如何塑造現代社會 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅琳鋼鐵:食物如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問過 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視為理所當然 , 如果我們走進一間商店、餐廳 , 或甚至走進戲院的門廳 , 在大約一小時內 , 那裡將會有食物等著我們 , 神奇地從某處冒出來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為 , 每一天 , 倫敦這麼大的城市 , 足夠的食物必須被生產、運輸、購買、販售、烹煮、吃、丟棄 , 類似的事情 , 每天都要發生在地球上的每個城市中 , 餵飽的城市是很了不起的 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們住在像這樣的地方 , 彷彿它們是世界上最自然的東西 , 忘記了我們是動物 , 我們需要進食 , 事實上 , 我們依賴大自然 , 就像我們古老的祖先一樣 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著更多人遷入城市 , 更多的自然世界被轉變為非凡的景觀 , 就像我身後的景觀 , 是巴西馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的景觀 , 但少數人見過這些景觀 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多這樣的景觀不僅僅是供給我們食物 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們愈來愈往城市 , 愈來愈多人在吃肉 , 全球每年有三分之一的穀物被餵食給動物 , 而不是給我們動物吃 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於它需要三倍的穀物實際上是十倍的穀物通過動物首先通過 , 餵養人類 , 這不是非常有效率的餵養方式 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個逐步的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	估計到了2050年 , 我們有兩倍的人口住在城市裡 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	據估計 , 肉類和乳製品會消耗兩倍之多 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	肉類和城市化正在逐漸興起 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會是一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到了2050年 , 六十億人挨餓的食肉動物 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 如果我們繼續下去 , 那我們就不太可能解決問題了 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有110萬公頃的熱帶雨林被砍掉 , 創造出新的耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時 , 我們也失去了相當於現有的可耕地 , 來鹽化和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也很渴望化石燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	西方每一卡路里所消耗的食物要耗約十卡路里 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	雖然我們花了很大的代價生產糧食 , 我們卻不珍視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國生產的一半食物目前都被丟棄了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	若要終結這些 , 在這漫長的過程中 , 我們甚至沒有妥善的管理來餵飽地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們當中有十億人過胖 , 同時也有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一點都不合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	想想看全球80%的糧食交易現在只由五家跨國企業來控制 , 這是很糟糕的圖片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們進入城市 , 世界也在擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 這是一種不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答這個問題稍微容易一些 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這個問題是古老近東地區的開端 , 也就是所謂的 「 肥沃冰淇淋 」 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是近期的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	它也很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 這裡有兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和城市主義 , 發生在同一個地方 , 同一時間 , 發生在同一個地方 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這並非偶然 , 因為農業和城市是相互連結的 。 它們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老祖先首次發現穀物的來源足夠大夠穩定足以支撐永久居住地
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些定居處是什麼樣子 , 我們會發現它們很緊密 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	它們被有生產力的農地包圍 , 由大型神廟群組成 , 像烏爾這樣的神廟 , 事實上 , 是精神化的 , 中央食品分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神殿安排收成 , 收集穀物 , 獻給眾神 , 接著提供給眾神的穀物 , 讓眾神不吃的穀物回饋給人民 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你願意 , 這些城市的精神和實體生活 , 主要是穀物和收穫 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老的城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是所有人都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	在西元前一個世紀 , 羅馬就有大約一百萬個公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市要如何餵飽自己 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是 , 我稱之為 「 古代食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬可以接觸到海洋 , 這使得羅馬可以從很遠的地方進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在遠古時期唯一可行的方法 , 因為要把食物運送到路上是非常困難的 , 這條路很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物很快就壞掉了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地發動了戰爭 , 像是車禍和埃及 , 只為了取得他們的穀物儲備 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張實在是太長了 , 沒錯 , 是軍事化的購物速率 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提一下羅馬實際上是從倫敦出口牡蠣的一階段我覺得這很不凡
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	羅馬透過食慾塑造它的內陸 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業化前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看倫敦在17世紀的地圖 , 我們可以看到 , 它的穀物是從泰勒那裡出來的 , 沿著地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場就在城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	從他們身上走到便宜的道路 , 也就是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街道 , 你可以看出三百年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 魚也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	魚當然是從河裡進來的 。 同樣的道理 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 比林斯門是倫敦的魚市場 , 一直到1980年代中期才開始運作 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	仔細想想 , 這真的很特別 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他所有人都帶著手機到處走 , 看起來就像磚頭 , 聞起來像是港口裡的魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	另一件關於城市食物的事:一旦它進入城市的根源被建立起來 , 它們就幾乎不會移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類則截然不同因為動物可以走進城市
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦大部分的肉都來自西北部 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它來了 , 抵達倫敦西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常有名的肉市場 , 位於那裡 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽是從東安格利亞進來的 , 以此類推 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像天氣女子在做這件事 。 總之 , 鳥類用腳來保護牠們的腳 , 用小的帆布鞋子 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	當牠們到達便宜的東端時 , 牠們就在那兒被賣掉了 , 這就是牠們被稱為 「 家禽 」 的原因 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看一下在工業時代之前建造的任何城市地圖 , 你可以追蹤食物的來源 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物所形塑的 , 不僅僅是閱讀街道的名字 , 它給了你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在過去的日子裡 , 是你星期五去買魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也必須想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一能買到食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的畫面你會發現你住在這樣的城市很難知道你的食物從何而來
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你的午餐時間是星期日 , 你可能三天前在你的窗外 , 心情或大聲流血 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是個有機城市 , 是有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的照片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 最早的火車旅客中有一些是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場了 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	它們被從視覺和思想中被屠殺 , 在鄉間的某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們用鐵路進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 它是第一次可以在任何地方種植真正的大小和形狀的城市 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去城市被地理限制 ; 以前 , 城市必須用非常困難的身體方法來取得它們的食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們就從地理上解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所見 , 從倫敦地圖上的這些地圖 , 在火車來臨的九十年後 , 它從一個很容易餵飽的小點 , 由動物來到這裡 , 如此一來 , 大量的噴泉 , 很難餵飽任何一隻腳的人 , 不論是動物或人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 火車來了汽車之後 , 這個過程就結束了 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市的最後解放 , 完全來自與大自然的明顯關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是沒有嗅覺的城市 , 沒有混亂 , 當然也沒有人 , 因為沒有人會夢想在這樣的地景中走路 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們為了獲取食物 , 開車到郊區的一個箱子裡 , 帶著一週的購物回來 , 想知道該拿它怎麼辦 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	此時此刻 , 我們與食物和城市的關係 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡有曾經是城市中心 , 周邊城市的社交核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	過去是一場社交活動 , 購買和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會做菜 , 現在只要加水 , 或加一點蛋 , 如果你要做蛋糕的話 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只需要讀包裝背後的標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不珍視食物 , 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	我們不再重視它 , 而是把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品體系最諷刺的是 , 他們做出了他們所承諾的事 , 讓事情變得更容易 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由在任何地方和任何地方建立城市 , 實際上 , 它們已經讓我們遠離了最重要的關係 , 那就是我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	而且它們也讓我們依賴只有它們能提供的系統 , 如我們所見 , 它們是不可持續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們該怎麼辦呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前湯瑪斯就這麼問自己了 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他《烏托邦》的首頁 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	它是一系列半自給自足的城邦 , 如果聽起來很熟悉 , 一個日子走在一起 , 每個人基本上都是農業 , 在自家後園種蔬菜 , 一起吃公共餐點等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你們可以說食物是烏托邦的基本原則即使絕對不是這樣
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	還有另一個著名的 「 烏托邦 」 遠景 , 伊內斯•霍華德的 「 花園城市 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列半自給自足的城邦 , 周圍有大都市化的小東西 , 被鐵路連接在一起 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次 , 食物可以被說是他的願景的原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來 , 但與默斯克韋茲的願景無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這些烏托邦的點子問題就在於烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是一個湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	有點開玩笑 , 因為希臘語有雙重衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它的意思可能是好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為它是理想的 。 它是想像的 。 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 用來思考人類居住的深層問題 , 讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 即希托邦 , 來自古希臘文 , 「 希托斯 」 代表食物 , 和 「 topos 」 等地點 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西索比亞 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物形塑的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以用食物當作一個非常強大的工具 , 一個概念性的工具 , 設計工具 , 來改變世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	如果我們這樣做 , 希托邦會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	嗯 , 我想看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 它只是狗臉上的表情 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	總之 , 這是生活的中心 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌 , 被享受 , 人們花時間來讚頌 。
this is where food should be in our society .	食物就在我們的社會裡 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但除非有像這樣的人 , 否則你不可能有這樣的場景 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順道一提 , 這些也可以是男性 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	就是那些想著食物的人 , 他們想著未來 , 計畫著 , 可以盯著一堆原料蔬菜 , 並且認得這些蔬菜 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 。 我們是網絡的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這樣的人 , 我們就不可能有這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我刻意選擇這個 , 因為它是一個男人在買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網絡 , 當地食物的市場 。
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	它是城市社交生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為沒有了這些 , 你就無法擁有這種地方 , 當地種植的食物 , 同時也是景觀的一部分 , 不只是一塊零和的商品 , 在看不見的地獄裡 。
cows with a view .	牛隻帶著景觀 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸氣堆積的 「 嗡 」 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把整個過程整合起來 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	它是溫室 , 孩子們會告訴所有關於食物和食物的知識 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有個叫做凱文的植物 , 或者它是屬於凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	總之 , 這種企劃將我們與大自然重新連結的專案非常重要 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 希托邦 , 對我來說 , 是一種看待的方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 意識到希托邦已經存在於小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅是要加入他們 , 用食物當作一種看待的方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們就不會再把城市視為是大型、大都市化、沒有生產力的團體 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 作為生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們無可避免地成為連結的一部分 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這也不是很棒的圖像 , 因為我們需要不再像現在這樣生產食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更深入思考永續栽培 , 這也是為什麼我認為這張影像可以為我做個總結 , 認為我們需要採取行動 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	它是一種重新思考食物如何塑造我們的生活方式 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道最棒的影像來自650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	安布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂的《好政府的寓言》 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點是城市和鄉間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這句話非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 這個國家會照顧這個城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在要問大家 , 如果他今天畫這張圖 , 安布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂會怎麼畫 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	一個良好政府的寓言今日會是什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	我們得要問這個問題 , 我們得要開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃什麼 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解 , 世界也是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採取這個想法 , 我們可以用食物作為一個非常強大的工具 , 來改善這個世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	從慈悲憲章開始的幾週後 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯研究了宗教在二十一世紀的角色:它的教條會把我們分開嗎 ? 還是讓我們團結起來 ? 她會檢視能夠驅動世界信仰的催化劑 , 重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	神、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal2009年的暴力、暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:咱們先恢復一下黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我一直覺得很挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我開始敏銳地意識到同情心的中心思想 , 在世界上主要的宗教信仰 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都進化出他們自己的 「 黃金法則 」 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時它會出現在正面的版本中 , 「 總是在對待別人 , 就像你想要被對待自己一樣 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 「 不要對其他人做你不希望他們做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的內心 , 發現讓你痛苦的事 , 然後在任何情況下拒絕 , 讓任何人痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調同情的重要性 , 不僅是因為它聽起來很好 , 也因為它有效 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了黃金法則如孔子所說的: 「 一整天 , 每一天 」 , 不只是做好事 , 然後返回貪婪和自我主義的生活 , 而是一整天都在做 , 把自己從世界的中心位置 , 放到另一邊 , 然後超越自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	這就帶你到一個名為 「 神 」 、 「 涅盤 」 、 「 拉瑪 」 、 「 道 」 的境界 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的自我意識 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道這對宗教生活而言是如此重要
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些很棒的例外 , 通常當宗教人士聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖聚在一起 , 他們會爭論深奧的教義 , 或是說出仇恨的議會或歧視同性戀或類似的事情 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們不太想有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在和一群宗教人士談話時 , 有點像是不停的表達方式 , 跨越他們的臉孔 , 因為人們通常都希望是對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然會打敗運動的對象 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我如此感激ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們溫柔地帶領我從我的書中學習 , 帶我進入21世紀 , 讓我能夠和比我想像中更廣大的觀眾對話 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我覺得這很迫切 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不打算在全球實施黃金法則 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 都一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 來傳遞給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代最偉大的任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球性社會 , 如我所說 , 在那裡 , 人們可以和平共處 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而要做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 卻被視為是問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 宗教不只是相信黃金法則的人 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種富有想像力的行為 , 將你自己置於他人之處 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 似乎對我而言 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續提出或強調我們的信仰的教條和不寬容的面向 , 或者我們也可以回到拉比 。 拉比希爾 , 較老的耶穌現代人 , 當普根要求他用一條腿站立時 , 總結整個猶太教教學 , 他說: 「 你很討厭哪一個 , 不要對你的鄰居做 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那就是托拉和其他一切都只是評論 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	猶太教的早期父親和教會的早期父親都說 , 任何對聖經的詮釋 , 都是不合法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要恢復那個精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只因為愛的精神將我們瓦解 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們得要讓它成真 , 我們能用ted介紹的現代溝通來做到 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經非常激動所有伴侶的反應 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 有一群人要用憲章來治癒新加坡社會的分裂 , 一些國會議員想要用政治的方式來實現它 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一個藝術展覽 , 在這展覽中 , 頂尖的藝術家會帶領人們、年輕人 , 並向他們展示 , 同情心也在所有藝術的根源上 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林團體舉辦活動和討論 , 正在討論伊斯蘭和所有信仰的中心思想 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能就此停止 。 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教的教誨 , 我們走錯了這條路 , 只專注於相信深奧的教義 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教誨必須採取行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	直到我臨終前 , 我都打算要做這件事 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我希望與我們的夥伴繼續做兩件事 , 來教育和刺激同情心思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們失去了同情心
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常常認為這只是對一個人感到抱歉 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但如果你只是想一想 , 你就不了解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須去做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望媒體參與其中 , 因為媒體很重要 , 幫助我們解決一些別人刻板印象的觀點 , 這些觀點讓我們彼此分裂 。
the same applies to educators .	教育家也是一樣 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能夠感受到動態、動態和挑戰富有同情心的生活方式 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到它需要急性智能 , 而不只是愚蠢的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想呼籲學者去探索他們自己和他人傳統中的同情心主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許最重要的是要鼓勵對無情演講的敏感度 , 這麼一來 , 因為有憲章 , 不論他們的信仰或缺少 , 他們都覺得有能力去挑戰不滿的言論 , 不論他們的宗教領袖、他們的政治領袖、產業領袖 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過要把憲章放上網 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍然被困在舊世界中 , 一群人坐在一間房間裡 , 卻又發表了另一種神奇的聲明 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted向我介紹一種全新的思維方式以及展示想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這就是ted美妙的地方 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有這些專業知識 , 如果我們能全部加入 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 有些時候 , 問題似乎很容易解決 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	最後我想引用一位英國作者 , 牛津作家的話 , 我不太常引用c.s.路易斯 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一句話 , 從我還是個學者的時候 , 一直牢牢牢記在我腦海中 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的書《四大愛》中 。
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他區分愛情 , 當兩個人凝視、拼字 , 彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	然後他把這個和友誼比起來 , 當兩個人站在一旁時 , 雙手肩並肩 , 雙眼固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信不疑 。
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	在我們對於調查的小小意見中 , 我強烈感受到 , 當所有不同的人團結在一起 , 為共同的目標努力 , 一起努力 , 差異就融化了 。
and we learn amity .	我們學會了 「 性 」 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會了一起生活 , 去認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	davidmacaulay重新經歷了一場風潮 , 有時也經歷了超現實的旅程 , 走向羅馬時代的完整旅程 , 他闡明了對歷史城市的敬意 。
macarthur grant , art , arts , book , cities , communication , culture , design , entertainment , humor , storytelling	麥克阿瑟•格蘭特、藝術、藝術、書、城市、通訊、文化、設計、娛樂、幽默、說故事、通訊、城市、通訊、文化、設計、娛樂、幽默、幽默、說故事、說故事 。
i draw to better understand things .	我畫畫 , 是為了更好的理解事物 。
sometimes i make a lot of drawings and i still don't understand what it is i'm drawing .	有時我畫了很多圖 , 但我仍然不知道我在畫什麼 。
those of you who are comfortable with digital stuff and even smug about that relationship might be amused to know that the guy who is best known for " the way things work , " while preparing for part of a panel for called understanding , spent two days trying to get his laptop to communicate with his new cd burner .	在座如果有人對數位產品感到自在 , 甚至對那段關係感到自在 , 可能會覺得很有趣 , 知道 「 事情運作的方式 」 , 同時也在準備一部分所謂的 「 理解 」 , 花了兩天的時間 , 試圖讓他的筆記型電腦和他的新cd燒錄器溝通 。
who knew about extension managers ?	誰知道延伸經理 ?
i've always managed my own extensions so it never even occurred to me to read the instructions , but i did finally figure it out . i had to figure it out , because along with the invitation came the frightening reminder that there would be no projector , so bringing those carousels would no longer be necessary but some alternate form of communication would .	我一直掌握著自己的延伸 , 所以從來沒有想過要看指示 , 但我終於想通了 。 我必須弄清楚 , 因為隨著邀請的來臨 , 提醒我沒有投影機 , 所以 , 把這些收容器帶回來是不必要的 , 但一些替代的交流形式就不必要了 。
now , i could talk about something that i'm known for , something that would be particularly appropriate for many of the more technically minded people here , or i could talk about something i really care about .	現在 , 我可以談談我所知的事 , 特別適合在座更專業的人 , 或者我可以談談我真正關心的事 。
i decided to go with the latter .	我決定帶著後者去 。
i'm going to talk about rome .	我要談談羅馬 。
now , why would i care about rome , particularly ?	為什麼我特別在乎羅馬 ?
well , i went to rhode island school of design in the second half of the '60s to study architecture .	嗯 , 我在羅德島設計學院念的是60年代後半的研究建築
i was lucky enough to spend my last year , my fifth year , in rome as a student . it changed my life .	我很幸運 , 能在去年、第五年、在羅馬擔任學生 。 這改變了我的一生 。
not the least reason was the fact that i had spent those first four years living at home , driving into risd everyday , driving back .	最不是因為我花了頭四年住在家裡每天開車到risd開車回家
i missed the '60s . i read about them ; i understand they were pretty interesting . i missed them , but i did spend that extraordinary year in rome , and it's a place that is never far from my mind .	我錯過了1960年代 , 我讀到他們 , 我知道他們很有趣 。 我錯過了他們 , 但我真的在羅馬度過了那不平凡的一年 , 那個地方從來沒有我這麼想過 。
so , whenever given an opportunity , i try to do something in it or with it or for it .	所以 , 不論何時給予機會 , 我都試著在其中做些什麼 , 或為它做點什麼 。
i also make drawings to help people understand things .	我也會畫圖 , 來協助大家了解事物 。
things that i want them to believe i understand .	我希望他們能相信我所理解的事物 。
and that's what i do as an illustrator , that's my job .	身為插畫家 , 我的工作就是這樣 。
so , i'm going to show you some pictures of rome .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些羅馬的照片 。
i've made a lot of drawings of rome over the years .	這些年來 , 我畫了很多關於羅馬的圖 。
these are just drawings of rome . i get back as often as possible i need to .	這些只是羅馬的圖畫 。 我盡可能多回去 。
all different materials , all different styles , all different times , drawings from sketchbooks looking at the details of rome .	所有不同的材質、不同風格、不同時代的畫作都在看羅馬的細節 。
part of the reason i'm showing you these is that it sort of helps illustrate this process i go through of trying to figure out what it is i feel about rome and why i feel it .	我之所以向你們展示這些 , 是因為它有助於說明我所經歷的這個過程 , 試圖找出我對羅馬的感受 , 以及我為什麼會感受到它 。
these are sketches of some of the little details .	這些是一些細節的草圖 。
rome is a city full of surprises .	羅馬是個充滿驚喜的城市 。
i mean , we're talking about unusual perspectives , we're talking about narrow little winding streets that suddenly open into vast , sundrenched piazzas never , though , piazzas that are not humanly scaled .	我的意思是 , 我們談的是不尋常的觀點 , 我們談的是狹窄的小小的風街 , 突然間變成廣闊、陽光充足的廣場 , 從來沒有人性化的廣場 。
part of the reason for that is the fact that they grew up organically .	部分原因是他們有機地長大 。
that amazing juxtaposition of old and new , the bits of light that come down between the buildings that sort of create a map that's traveling above your head of usually blue especially in the summer compared to the map that you would normally expect to see of conventional streets .	新舊和新舊之間的神奇對立 , 建築物之間的位元光線 , 有點像是在你腦海上方移動 , 通常是藍色的 , 特別是在夏天 , 相較於你平常看到的地圖 。
and i began to think about how i could communicate this in book form .	我開始思考要如何用書本來溝通 。
how could i share my sense of rome , my understanding of rome ?	我要如何分享我對羅馬的感受 , 我對羅馬的理解 ?
and i'm going to show you a bunch of dead ends , basically .	基本上我會給你們看一堆死胡同 。
the primary reason for all these dead ends is when if you're not quite sure where you're going , you're certainly not going to get there with any kind of efficiency .	所有這些死胡同的主要原因是如果你不太確定你要去哪裡 , 你絕對不會達到那樣的效率 。
here's a little map . and i thought of maps at the beginning ; maybe i should just try and do a little atlas of my favorite streets and connections in rome .	這是一張小地圖 。 一開始我想到了地圖 ; 也許我應該試著在羅馬最愛的街道和連接上做些小地圖 。
and here's a line of text that actually evolves from the exhaust of a scooter zipping across the page .	這一系列的文字其實是從一個小摩托車橫跨頁面的廢氣中演化出來的 。
here that same line of text wraps around a fountain in an illustration that can be turned upside down and read both ways .	這一行的文字包圍著噴泉 , 用圖表可以顛倒過來閱讀和閱讀兩種方式 。
maybe that line of text could be a story to help give some human aspect to this .	也許這一行的文字可以是一個故事 , 來協助我們對此有一些人性的觀點 。
maybe i should get away from this map completely , and really be honest about wanting to show you my favorite bits and pieces of rome and simply kick a soccer ball in the air which happens in so many of the squares in the city and let it bounce off of things . and i'll simply explain what each of those things is that the soccer ball hits .	也許我應該完全脫離這張地圖 , 誠實的說 , 想讓你們看看我最喜歡的羅馬地點 , 然後在城市裡的許多廣場上踢足球 , 讓它彈走 。 我來解釋一下 , 足球擊中了什麼 。
that seemed like a sort of a cheap shot .	這似乎是個很便宜的畫面 。
but even though i just started this presentation , this is not the first thing that i tried to do and i was getting sort of desperate .	但即使我剛開始這場演說 , 這不是我嘗試做的第一件事 , 我有點急得絕望 。
eventually , i realized that i had really no content that i could count on , so i decided to move towards packaging .	最終 , 我意識到我沒有什麼可以依靠的內容 , 所以我決定去做包裝 。

but one of the ideas that emerged from some of those sketches was the notion of traveling through rome in different vehicles at different speeds in order to show the different aspects of rome .	但從這些草圖中衍生出來的一個想法是旅行在不同的交通工具中穿越羅馬 , 以展現羅馬的不同面向 。
sort of an overview of rome and the plan that you might see from a dirigible .	有點像是羅馬的總觀 , 和你從可怕的角度來看的計劃 。
quick snapshots of things you might see from a speeding motor scooter , and very slow walking through rome , you might be able to study in more detail some of the wonderful surfaces and whatnot that you come across .	快速拍攝你可能在摩托車上看到的東西 , 非常慢的步行穿越羅馬 , 你可能可以更詳細地研究一些美妙的表面 , 你碰到的事物 。
anyways , i went back to the dirigible notion .	總之 , 我回到了可怕的想法 。

this gives me a chance to suggest to you the structure of the column of marcus aurelius , which is really no more than a pile of quarters high thick quarters . over the piazza of saint ignacio , completely ruining the symmetry , but that aside a spectacular place to visit .	這給了我一個機會來建議馬可•奧里烏斯圓柱的結構 , 這真的不是一堆四分之一高厚的四分之一 。 在聖伊那西比的廣場上 , 完全毀了對稱性 , 但除此之外還有一個很壯觀的地方 。

unfortunately for her , the anchor line gets tangled around the feet of some boy scouts who are visiting the pantheon , and they are immediately yanked out and given an extraordinary but terrifying tour of some of the domes of rome , which would , from their point of view , naturally be hanging upside down .	不幸的是 , 主流線纏住了一些男孩的腳 , 他們正在參觀萬神殿 , 他們立刻被拉出來 , 帶了一趟非凡卻又駭人的旅程 , 參觀羅馬的一些穹頂 , 從他們的角度看 , 羅馬的頭頂上會自然而然地倒著 。

removes some scaffolding . one of the reasons rome remains the extraordinary place it is that because of scaffolding and the determination to maintain the fabric , it is a city that continues to grow and adapt to the needs of the particular time in which it finds itself , or we find it .	除去一些支架 。 羅馬依然保留非凡之地的理由之一 , 就是因為鷹架和維持布料的決心 , 羅馬依然生長並適應特定時間的需求 , 或我們發現它 。
right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	透過廣場德拉•羅頓達 , 在萬神廟的前面 , 再次殘破不堪 , 最後終於成功了 。

that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是我第一次嘗試 , 但似乎還不夠傳達我想要傳達的關於羅馬的任何事 。

and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我只會拿我最喜歡的位元和碎片 , 把它們放到萬神廟內 , 保持它的規模 , 這樣你就可以看見聖地華的頂端 , 西斯提烏斯的金字塔 , 以及巴拉曼特的暫時座落在這個不可思議的地方 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這只是一幅畫 , 所以我想也許是時候讓皮蘭西認識escher了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你可以看到我開始失去控制權 , 也失去了希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條很薄的藍色疲勞路線 , 會貫穿整條路徑 , 讓路線連接在一起 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不僅僅是用來收集和儲存資訊的好方法 , 它是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層一層剝離 , 我們認為它們是頁面 , 用某種方式做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們想成是層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是個水平層、垂直層次的地方 , 我心想 , 只要剝下一張頁面 , 就可以讓我去思考 , 如果我能用正確的方式來呈現它 , 可以讓我呈現出它的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部分建築物牆上的黏土覆蓋了這些疤 ; 數世紀以來 , 隨著這些建築的改造而不是被拆掉 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺紙頁 , 讓你把它展開 , 你可以看到我所謂的傷疤組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 建造小窗戶是不可或缺的 , 因為壞人會來 , 或其他什麼的 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應一切都埋藏在黏土之下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這張palazzo的頁面給你們看看裡面發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我也能向各位展示 , 那些壯觀的建築物的角落 , 和那些巨大的石塊 , 或用磚塊和黏土做成的假石塊 , 通常是比較常見的 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它變得有點立體 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把你從一條狹窄的小街上帶到其中一個令人驚訝的廣場 , 只要用一個雙扇摺疊的紙張 , 如果你像我一樣小時候讀一本彈出的書 , 希望你會把頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把腦袋包起來 , 就在那個廣場上 , 就在那短暫的時間內 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我其實沒有做任何比摺紙更複雜的事 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但接著我想 , 也許我可以簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	咱們來看看萬神廟和廣場德拉•羅頓達在它面前 。
here's a book completely wide open .	這本書是完全開放的 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不整體打開這本書 , 如果我把它打開90度 , 我們會向下看著萬神殿的正面 , 我們會看到上面 , 或多或少在正方形上 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把書翻過來 , 我們就在萬神廟的正面 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有任何戲法只是本不完全打開的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這看似很有希望 。 我心想 , 也許我會把它內部做出來 , 我甚至可以把摺痕和唯一部分開放的書做結合 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以我們進入了萬神廟 , 它會不斷地成長 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我在對的軌道上 , 但它似乎失去了它的人性 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想讓大家注意一本書 , 一路上收集資訊 , 那一定是件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 讓我大吃一驚 ,
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果那是隻寄生鴿 , 它會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是這趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果標題是可行的 , 使用它 。 但這將會是一個穿越羅馬的旅程 , 展示我喜愛的羅馬的一切 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	一隻鴿子坐在教堂的上方 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天休息了 , 做些正常的鴿子事 。 回來了 , 整個地方都被鷹架和綠色網路包覆著 , 沒有辦法讓這隻鴿子回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在是隻無家可歸的鴿子 , 它必須找個適合居住的地方 , 這樣才能讓我通過我最愛的目錄 , 我們從較高的鴿子開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回去和家人住在一起 ; 這不是一件好事 , 但它確實能讓鴿子再次聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有一個人應該用某種方式參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 他一輩子都在照顧生病鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方去找他們危險的地方 , 什麼都不會 , 他們和這個傢伙變成朋友 , 學會幫他做把戲 , 在午餐時間給他娛樂 , 諸如此類 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	有一種真實的連結存在於這個老人和這些鴿子之間 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事結束時病得很重 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教他們拼他的名字 , 阿爾多 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三、四天沒見到他之後出現了 , 他住在這個小車庫裡 , 拼他的名字 , 飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於有了足夠的力量 , 能爬上梯子到屋頂上 , 所有鴿子 , 紅氣球 , 都在等著他 , 然後他們把他帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到:每當他丟了一隻鴿子 , 他就會把那隻鴿子帶到城牆外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在古羅馬的習俗中 , 死者從來沒有埋藏在牆裡 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這是個很棒的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這將會有很長的路要走 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了...再說一次 , 如果包裝沒有用 , 如果故事沒有傳播到任何地方 , 我只想出了標題 , 希望標題能把我踢向正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時候它的確會把我集中起來 , 我甚至會畫一個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是書名版 , 最終讓我找到了解決方案 , 故事是關於一位年輕女子 , 她把信息傳遞給一位在羅馬城牆外的人 , 給城市裡的一個人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	這隻鴿子正飛過阿帕尼亞山脈上方
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墳墓和松果 , 一路上都是如此 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你看到鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不到紅線 , 你就是鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時此刻 , 必須要盡可能地傳達出那種感覺 , 那種感覺會像飛越城市而不動的感覺 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過了cestius的金字塔--你會覺得很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬 , 超越了大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這有點不尋常 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件最讓人敬畏的鴿子不會做的事:它需要一條景象路線 , 我覺得這個裝置必須要真的將這本書延伸到四頁以外 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	我們繞著羅馬競技場盤旋 , 穿越了西班牙聖母堂 , 以及海克力士神殿 , 朝著河流前進 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎與palazzofarnis設計的米開朗基羅大道相撞 , 用羅馬競技場的石頭建造出來的 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯瞰柬埔寨的fiori 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事 , 因為這是完全不合乎規則的觀點 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的觀點規則是如果它看起來可信 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出消失點在哪裡 ; 這裡有幾個在火星上 , 還有幾個在克雷莫納 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在廣場前面 , 在聖母堂前方 , 在那裡 , 一場足球比賽正在進行 , 我們被足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是被足球擊中的可怕畫面 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的部分:聖母堂的速度 , 足球 , 鳥翅膀上沒有任何變化 , 所以我必須重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想看聖母院的速度 , 這些書非常靈活 , 非常互動 , 只要轉過身去 , 用另一種方式來看它 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過這條小巷 , 我們可以看到影響力被記錄在紅線上 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	然後鳥兒藉由中世紀的塔樓把自己拉到一座中世紀的塔上 , 向聖地卡恩斯教堂及其周圍的中世紀塔樓靠近 , 向下看向廣場navona , 我們已經看到並飛過好幾次了 ; 伯尼斯雕像有四條河流 , 然後經過美麗的布羅米諾瓦索 , 在26英尺深的天孔上停下來 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著 , 我們會不斷地轉動 , 因為我們在飛行 , 我們不用擔心在這個時刻的重力 , 這樣一幅圖就能在頁面上隨心所欲地轉換 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們穿越gesu時 , 我們會有點開心 ; 用這種方式模仿建築並不讓人意外 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	經過這座美麗的牆 , 充滿了我剛才提到的混合體 ; 美麗的雕刻裝置在 「 崛起 」 的牆上 , 諸如此類 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後 , 我們到達了帕拉索的庭院 , 那是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓 , 在那裡有人在畫板工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他從鳥的腿上移除這條訊息 , 這是牠所說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著畫板 , 我們會看到他正在畫的是鴿子走過的旅程地圖 , 紅線延伸穿過所有的畫面 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要資訊 , 這樣我們才能完成理解的循環 , 你只需要讀讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
