mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究員skylartibbits在自我組裝上工作--這個想法是:與其建造東西 , 我們可以創造出可以自己製造的東西 , 就像一股dnazips本身一樣 。 這是一個很大的概念 。 tibbits告訴我們三個關於自我組裝未來可能是什麼樣子的計劃 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylarltibbits:我們能製造出能製造自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天 , 我想向各位展示未來我們製造東西的方式 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快我們的建築物和機器就會自行組合、複製、修復它們自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要讓你們看看我認為目前的製造業狀態 , 然後將它與一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 50萬到百萬個部分 , 相當複雜、令人興奮的新技術鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空--250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈秒折疊 , 或是有三十億鹼基對的dna , 我們可以在大約一個小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統中有這麼多複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠超過任何我們可以建造的東西 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建造的東西 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們的效率更高 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 自然系統有一點超級有趣 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以把它翻譯成我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們建造東西的方式就有令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想在我們的物理環境中使用自組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 讓我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是建築物如何運作的dna
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的零件 , 可以用這序列來摺疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能激活這些能量 , 讓我們的零件能夠折疊程式 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的錯誤修正冗餘 , 以確保我們已經成功地建構出我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些計畫 , 我在麻省理工學院的同事和我正在努力實現這個自組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	第一兩種是巨型機器人和決策機器人 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些計畫是大規模的可重組的機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們被機械電子設備和感應器嵌入其中 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你解碼你想摺什麼 , 變成一連串的角度--負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120--類似這樣的東西 ; 一連串的角度 , 或轉彎 , 然後你把這個序列列列列送進去 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每一個單位都帶著它的消息--負120--它會旋轉 , 檢查它是否到達那裡 , 然後把它傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 致力於這個專案 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我想這真的能帶來光明:這真的可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 很多男人小時都為了這個八英呎的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個規模擴大嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人嵌入到每個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題是 , 看看被動的本質 , 或是被動地試圖重新配置可編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 它嘗試著實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上是最基本的計算元件 , 數位邏輯閘 , 直接嵌入到你的零件當中 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是一個nand大門 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個四面體 , 就是門 , 會做你的計算 , 你有兩個輸入四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 正如你在建構你的磚塊一樣 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一種是從先前被安置的磚塊中來的 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會給你一個3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著 , 使用者可以開始插入他們想要的磚塊裡 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算它以前的做法 , 以及你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 向上或向下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	在左手邊 , [1 , 1]輸入等於0 , 輸入值會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入1輸出 , 就會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	那真正的意思是 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的東西的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們擁有所有被建構出來的信息 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個例子中 , 我稱它為自導複製 , 因為你的結構包含了確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代某部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有本地資訊都嵌入在上面 , 告訴你如何修正它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以擁有爬上去讀的東西 , 並且在一對一輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它被直接嵌入 ; 沒有任何外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	最後我要展示的項目叫做偏見鏈 , 它可能是我們目前被動自組裝系統中最令人興奮的例子 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它需要可重組性和可編程性 , 讓它成為完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每一個元素都完全相同 , 且它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每條鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要向右或向左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你是在告訴每個單位是否應該向左或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈時 , 它會折疊成任何你編程的配置 , 在這個例子中 , 一個螺旋 , 或者 , 在這個例子中 , 兩個立方體彼此相鄰 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以基本上你可以設計任何立體形狀或單面的二維空間 , 完全被動地進入這條鏈中 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們什麼關於未來 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我想這告訴我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復我們的實體結構、建築物、機器都有新的可能性 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些地區有新的可編程性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那裡你就有了新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚塊都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是驚人的平行電腦運算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	對此 , 很讓人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我剛剛展示的這些專案只是邁向未來的一小步 , 如果我們將這些新技術實施在一個新的自組裝世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 我們繪製了大陸地圖 , 我們甚至去過海底深處兩次 。 下一代要探索什麼 ? 生物學家和探險家納森•沃菲提出了這個答案:幾乎所有事情 。 我們都可以開始 , 他說 , 帶著看不見的微小世界開始探索 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、科學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃爾菲:還有什麼要去探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮耀一位偉大的二十世紀探險家 , roychapmanandrews 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他美國自然歷史博物館中andrews引領一系列探險未知區域就像這裡的gobi沙漠
he was quite a figure .	他是個很棒的人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	據說 , 他後來成為印第安那瓊斯角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我對一群中學學生演講 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 如果有任何東西比在ted演講還要嚇人的話 , 它會試著把焦點放在一群12歲的12歲小朋友的注意力中 , 留在45分鐘的講座上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演講結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但有一個問題在那之後就一直困在我身上 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 我們很多人有意識到 , 地球的偉大探索時代已經結束了 , 下一代他們得要去外太空 , 或深海 , 才能找到有意義的東西去探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上真的沒有什麼值得我們去探索的重要嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回想起生物學史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以 , beijerinck開始發現菸草鑲嵌疾病的起因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是從菸草植物中取出受感染的汁液 , 並通過更小的過濾器過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	到達那時 , 他覺得一定有什麼東西比當時所知最小的生命形式還要小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘經紀人命了個名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 的拉丁文 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭露病毒的過程中 , beijerinck為我們開啟了一個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒組成地球上絕大多數的基因信息 , 比所有其他形式生命形式的基因信息加起來還多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 世界上已經有大量的實用應用 , 像是天花的消滅 , 預防子宮頸癌疫苗的出現 , 我們現在知道大部分是由人類乳突病毒所引起的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們不知道組成地球上大部分基因信息的生命型態 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索未知的世界 , 像是深度定序 , 讓我們能做的 , 不僅僅是滑翔表面 , 去看特定物種的個別基因組 , 還能檢視整個次元 , 即將微生物帶入我們體內、周圍 , 以及記錄所有這些物種的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用在從土壤到皮膚中間的一切 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們現在定期這樣做 , 來找出未知爆發的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上取下鼻腔代謝 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們通常會尋找呼吸道病毒 , 像是流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到非常大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究基因信息 , 我們會看到一些常見的懷疑--當然 , 很多人類的遺傳信息 , 還有細菌和病毒的信息 , 主要是從你鼻子裡完全沒有傷害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了非常非常令人驚訝的東西 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 你鼻子中大約20%的基因信息與我們以前從未見過的東西不符合 , 沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對我們這些研究這種數據的小組而言 , 我們當中有些人開始稱之為資訊生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是我們以前看過的 ; 它有點像是我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多類似的例子 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子裡有20%的基因信息是很多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對比較無菌的血液中 , 大約百分之一到二的信息是暗物質無法被分類 , 無法和我們以前看到的任何東西匹配或匹配 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們以為這可能是人造的 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著它們變得愈來愈準確 , 我們已經確定這些資訊是一種生命形式 , 至少當中有一些是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設 , 只是在嬰兒期 , 卻存在著非常令人興奮的可能性:埋藏在生命中 , 遺傳信息中 , 是生命中尚未被辨識的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一系列a、t、c、g時 , 我們可能會發現一種全新的生命類型 , 像beijerinck , 會從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	也許這能讓我們找出折磨我們的癌症成因 , 或是辨識出我們不熟悉的爆發病源頭 , 或是創造出分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣布 , 與史丹佛、加州理工學院和加州大學舊金山分校的同事一起 , 我們正開始著手探索生物暗物質 , 以便探索新生命形式的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們意識到病毒 , 一種組成地球上大部分基因信息的生命形式 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚訝我們可能完全沒察覺到在我們眼前的新階級的新生命 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	的確 , 我們可能已經繪製了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能已經發現了所有的哺乳類動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有其他可以探索的生物 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同事為下一代的探險家提供了很重要的一課 , 像來自威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想 , 如果我們把這一課說出來 , 應該是這樣的:不要假設我們目前認為有的全部故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	去追尋你選擇去探索的任何領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊無所不知 , 他們只是等待被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇人物科學家大衛•德魯斯把理論物理學放在背上 , 討論一個更迫切的問題:我們物種的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	在我們的宇宙中 , 大衛•德魯斯克就在我們的位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出義肢 , 說出令人驚訝的話 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這麼做 , 但我想從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	事實上 , 第一種是有史以來最為人熟知的 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	也就是說 , 地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境等等 , 都是獨一無二的 , 可以維持我們的演化或創造 , 就像以前被認為的、現在的存在的那樣 , 最重要的是 , 我們的未來能存活 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今 , 這個想法有個戲劇性的名字: 「 地球太空船 」 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這裡的概念是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是充滿敵意的 , 內在是我們所擁有的一切 , 我們所仰賴的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件大家都知道的事 , 與人類歷史上大多數人所相信的相反 , 事實上 , 人類並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬•霍金說過的 , 我們只是一個典型的行星表面的化學污垢 , 繞著一個典型的恆星運行 , 位在一個典型的銀河系的郊區 , 諸如此類 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	首先 , 大家都知道的兩件事 , 有點像是在說 , 我們身處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的服裝等等 , 第二件事是說我們身在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	特別是如果你認為這兩者是深切的真理 , 要活下來 , 要告知你的人生決策 , 那麼它們似乎會互相衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能完全阻止兩者的出現 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是的 。 讓我從第二個開始:典型的 。 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 讓我們環顧四周 , 看看隨機方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學污垢 , 這一點也不典型 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你所要做的就是朝著同一個方向走幾百英哩 , 然後往回看 , 你不會看到任何牆或化學污垢 , 你只能看到一個藍色的行星 。 如果你再往遠處看 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為星星是從星系來的 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大多數地方 , 宇宙中典型的地方 , 都離任何星系都差不多 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們再進一步 , 直到我們在銀河之外 , 再回頭看 , 是的 , 巨大的銀河系中有螺旋手臂 , 擺在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時此刻 , 我們已經有十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍然離宇宙中典型的地方很近 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地點 , 你必須走一千倍到達星系間的空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那會是什麼樣子呢 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方長什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 代價很高 , ted安排了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 呈現了星系間空間--從星系間空間的角度 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	請把燈關掉 , 這樣我們就可以看見了嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不是很完美--你看 , 在星系間的空間中 , 漆黑了 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 如果你正看著離你最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星被炸成超新星 , 而你正直盯著它 , 當光照到你的時候 , 你仍然無法看見任何閃光 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙有多大、有多黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星是如此的明亮 , 非常傑出 , 它會讓你在好幾光年內死去 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但從星系間的空間 , 距離你甚至看不到這麼遠 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡也很冷 , 絕對零度以下不到三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它很空 , 真空中有一百萬倍的密度 , 比目前地球上最好的技術能產生的真空濃度要低一百萬倍 。 這就是典型的地方和這個地方是如此不同 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這個地方就是那麼的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	請把燈光放回去嗎 ? 謝謝
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在我們如何知道一個如此遙遠的環境 , 如此與眾不同 , 如此陌生 , 如此與眾不同的環境 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式--創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	這是什麼意思呢 ? 嗯 , 再往遠處看--我是指從這裡開始 , 利用望遠鏡你會看到看起來像星星的東西
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 方形 」 。 方形原本是指方形的物體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著有些東西看起來有點像星星 , 但不是星星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 十億年前 , 數十億光年之外 , 銀河系中心的物質向超大質量黑洞倒塌 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著強烈的磁場引導了重力崩塌的一些能量 。 有些物質以巨大的噴射流形式反射 , 照亮了葉片 , 並且我認為那是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理性質可能更不像這種噴射流的物理性 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法存活一瞬間 。 當語言試圖描述其中一次噴射流會是什麼樣子的時候 , 語言會崩解 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這有點像經歷超新星爆炸 , 但在時間軸上 , 數百萬年的時間 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這種噴射流發生得如此精確 , 幾十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 模型 , 預測 , 並且解釋 , 最重要的是 , 你在現實中所看到的現象 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另一個四邊形的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是表面的圖像 , 還包含了這個圖像 , 還包含了解釋性的模型 , 體現了相同的數學關係 , 以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 另一種結構與時間相似的信心就會隨著時間增加 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這樣的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	實體物體 , 不像它們之間那樣 , 儘管它們有著相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨著時間越來越長 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們是一個不一樣的化學污垢 。 這個化學污垢具有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構有越來越精準的結構 , 萬物的結構 。 這個地方 , 不是宇宙的其他地方 , 這個中心本身就包含了整個物理現實的結構和因果的本質 。 並且 , 遠遠不被忽視 , 物理定律允許這一切發生 , 甚至允許這發生 , 是物理世界中最重要的事之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	太陽系和環境 , 以我們的形式 , 如何取得與宇宙其他部分的這種特殊關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬•霍金的評論有一點是正確的 , 但它的重點是錯的 , 但它的重點在於它沒有任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有任何特殊的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟 。 它是有三樣東西存在的 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的一種形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一個電腦 , 沒有物質 , 就無法製造出一台電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體能夠有效地記錄我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 較不具體 , 但對於開放式知識和解釋的創造來說 , 同樣重要 , 就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境被證據淹沒了 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	比方說 , 牛頓的萬有引力定律在300年前就開始了
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但我們過去所做的證據 , 在幾十億年前 , 在地球上的每一平方公尺都落在地球上 , 且會在幾十億年後繼續下去 。 其他的科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	就我們所知 , 發現所有科學中最基本的真理 , 都在這裡 , 只為了我們星球上接收 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的所在地充滿了證據 , 還有物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 創造開放式知識的這三個前提條件是最低可能的 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	正如我所說的 , 它是空的、寒冷的、它是暗的、還是暗的 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另外一個狹隘的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個立方體在星系間空間中 , 和我們的家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在 , 立方體是以人類的標準來看的 , 但那仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造一個自給自足的太空站 , 這裡有一群科學家致力於創造一個開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 要把氫氣從星系間空間聚集在一起 , 再轉化成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但問題是 , 在一個完全可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麼 , 除了知道如何 , 還能防止我們去做這件事情 , 還能防止我們去做這件事呢 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是一個關於知識的問題 , 而不是資源的問題 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動供應能源 , 因為轉變會是核融合反應爐和證據呢 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	同樣的 , 這對人類的感官來說是黑暗的 。 但你要做的就是拿一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是今天的設計 , 向外看 , 然後你會看到跟我們這裡一樣的星系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你就能看見恆星和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在這些星系中 , 你能夠進行天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最困難的科學可能是生物學實地考察 , 因為要花數億年才能到達最近的有生命的星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我得告訴各位 , 抱歉 , 理查 , 但我從來不喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每隔幾億年就一次做一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間確實包含了所有開放式知識的前提條件 。 任何一個立方體 , 在宇宙中的任何一個角落 , 都可以成為一個中心 , 如果我們知道如何實現它的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們並不是唯一適宜居住的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間能夠創造出開放式的解釋流 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境都是如此 。 那地球也是污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	限制性因素 , 在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源豐富 , 而知識 , 是稀少的 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種以宇宙為基礎的知識觀點 , 或許--我認為應該讓我們感到非常特殊 。 但也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這也意味著 , 若沒有具體的知識 , 能夠生存下去 , 我們就不會生存下去 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要幾光年之外的超新星 , 我們就會死亡 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁•雷斯最近寫了一本書 , 內容是關於我們對各種事物的脆弱性 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出了差錯 , 最重要的是要用大規模殺傷性武器來恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為人類文明只有50%的機率能存活這個世紀 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他晚些時候會在研討會上談到這一點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為這個機率是正確的分類來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他的看法 , 我們可以生存 , 我們可以生存下來 , 我們可以生存下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否時間創造相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險不是史無前例的物種會絕種
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明就到此為止 , 絕大多數的物種和文明都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外 , 那麼邏輯上我們唯一的希望就是利用區分人類和文明的一個特徵以及其他所有事物的特徵--也就是 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋能力 , 新的知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	現在 , 讓我用這個做為當前的爭議 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而是要說明我是說什麼 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是那種物理學家 。 至於全球暖化 , 我只是一個層級的人 。 要做的事情是認真看待普遍的科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太遲了 , 無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為 , 如果我們目前最好的選擇就是用類似京都議定書的方式來預防二氧化碳排放 , 限制它的經濟活動 , 以及它數百億美元的成本 , 不論它是什麼 , 那已經是一場災難了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡導者所採取的行動 , 根本不是為了解決問題 , 只是稍微拖延一下 。 所以已經太遲了 , 以致於在任何人意識到危險之前就已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	可能在1970年代已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放正要降低數十億人會死亡的冰河時期 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	現在我學到的教訓似乎很清楚 , 我也不知道為什麼這不是公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們不能總是知道 。 當我們知道即將發生的災難時 , 以及如何以比災難本身的代價來解決問題 , 那麼其實沒有什麼爭論 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有任何預防措施 , 沒有任何預防原則 , 可以避免我們還未預知的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個解決問題的立場 , 而不僅僅是問題的立場 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	的確 , 一盎司的預防等於一磅的解藥 , 但那只是我們知道如何預防 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你鼻子被打了 , 那麼醫學的科學不會教你如何避免穿刺 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再只在預防上尋求解藥和專注 , 那麼它也幾乎無法達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前世界正在興起 , 計畫要用各種成本來強迫減少氣體排放 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要以計劃來降低溫度 , 並計劃在高溫下生存 , 不論花什麼成本 , 都要有效率且便宜 。 有些計劃存在 , 比如在太空中大量鏡子的鏡子來把陽光轉移開 , 鼓勵水生生物吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些都是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類努力解決這個問題的核心 , 也不是一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	在我們還沒有意識到的問題上 , 能夠正確解決問題的能力 , 不是無限期避免的好運 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩個石頭平板 , 雕刻在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一塊刻著: 「 問題是可解決的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	而在另一塊地上: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家要如何擺脫貧窮 , 如果它被困在一個不好的體制中 ? 經濟學家保羅羅羅默揭開了一個大膽的想法: 「 特區城市 」 , 「 城市規模管理區 」 , 由一個國家聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅羅•羅默的想法:特區城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個很棒的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的路燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我見過像他們這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	讓我們挑一個例子 , 那個穿綠色襯衫的 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字 , 尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我敢打賭尼爾森有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這就是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森有像手機一樣先進的科技 , 但卻無法取得一百歲的科技 , 來在家中產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡單來說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不良的規則可以預防雙贏的解決方案 , 只要人們能把新科技帶進來 , 讓像尼爾森這樣的人都可以使用 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	在這個國家的電力公司遵守一條規則 , 電力公司必須以非常低的補助金來銷售電力 , 事實上 , 電價非常低 , 每賣一單位都會損失金錢 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以資源和激勵措施都沒有 , 連接許多用戶都沒有 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這條規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他見識到 , 有另一套規則 , 規則是企業賺取小額利潤的規則 , 所以他們有動機要簽訂更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這就是尼爾森手機公司所遵守的規則 , 這種規則是尼爾森從下面營運的電話 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統知道這些規則是如何運作的 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變電價定律的規則 , 但他卻遇到了一場來自企業和消費者的抗議 , 他們想要維持現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他堅守規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森被困在路燈下讀書 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是 , 試著想出如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	有一些規則我們可以發展 , 來改變規則嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我認為有一種一般的抽象洞見可以讓我們實踐 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人們更多選擇 , 給予在許多國家中 , 領導者更多的選擇 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 介紹這兩者之間的對立是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能會想要給領導者這種選擇 , 例如給總統提高電價 , 移除經濟中人民想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續消耗補助電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你會產生張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能想辦法給雙方更多選擇 , 那就能給我們一系列改變規則的規則 , 讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也能上網 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則的破壞性效應 , 規則可以讓人們留在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署在夜晚拍攝的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 比起它的鄰居 , 它就像是個黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在你不會驚訝地發現北韓的規則使得人們陷入黑暗 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 要了解北韓和南韓起始於一模一樣的規則 , 不論是法律或法規 , 也要了解更深層的理解、規範、文化、價值觀 , 和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分離時 , 他們做出選擇 , 導致他們在規則上有非常不同的路徑 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以我們可以改變 , 人類可以改變我們和彼此互動的規則 , 不論是好是壞 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個加勒比海地區 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 在這裡 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很暗 , 相較於這裡的鄰居多明尼加共和國 , 居民數量也差不多 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	相較於波多黎各這兩個國家都很黑暗 , 居民數量只有海地或多明尼加共和國的一半是比較黑暗的 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是 , 體制之所以不好 , 是因為政府很軟弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只有那些規則是不好的 , 因為政府太強大、太壓迫 , 就像北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要創造出有良好規則的環境 , 我們就不能撕掉 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須想辦法建設 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國戲劇性地展示出與規則合作的潛在和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這張圖表的最初 , 中國是全球高科技領導人 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國有先驅的技術 , 像是鋼、列印、火藥 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採用 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則中 , 鼓勵傳播這些想法 , 一個獲利的動機 , 可以鼓勵傳播開來 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 減緩了創新 , 阻止了中國和世界其他地方的發展 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 作為世界上其他國家的創新 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 也發展新的規則 , 中國已經被阻止進步 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入停滯不前 , 因為它縮小了世界其他地方的收入 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的資料 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它繪製了中國的平均收入佔美國平均收入的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代 , 各位可以看到 , 大約只有3% 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末期 , 情況改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國經濟開始起飛 , 中國人開始很快地趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在晚上回到地圖上 , 會得到一個線索 , 來引導中國規則的劇烈改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的地方 , 各位可以在線的邊緣看到 , 是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀大部分的時候 , 都遵循著一套非常不同的規則運作 , 和當時其他大陸規則相比 , 這些規則都被當時的市場經濟所複製 , 被英國所管理 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個有數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸 , 到開始在工作 , 比如縫製襯衫、做玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了讓收入增加 , 技能越來越快的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個領導者 , 像是鄧小平可以複製的模型 , 當他們決定將整個大陸推向市場模式時 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫每個中國人立即轉向市場模式 , 他們採取的做法是創造一些特殊的區域 , 從某種意義上來說 , 英國採取的做法是:讓機會和市場規則合作 , 讓那些想參與其中的人能有機會參與 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港附近設立了四個特殊的經濟區 , 在那裡 , 中國人可以來工作 , 城市在很快的環境中成長 ; 外國企業也能來這裡做些事 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域有個叫做深圳的城市 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市 , 有台灣公司製造了你們許多人擁有的iphone , 他們用中國人的勞工 , 搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	在四個特區之後 , 有14個沿海城市 , 以相同的意義打開 , 最終在這些地方展現了成功 , 人們可以選擇進去 , 因為他們提供的優勢 , 他們聚在一起 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	證實了成功導致整個經濟體轉向市場模式的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在中國的例子顯示了幾點
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保留人民的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:運作的規模是正確的 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變一個村落的規則 , 你可以這麼做 , 但村落實在太小了 , 無法得到你所能得到的好處 , 如果你有數百萬人都在做好的規則 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你就不能給一些人機會 , 看看結果如何 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市讓你有機會創造出新的地方 , 有了新的規則 , 人們可以選擇 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	當數百萬人以良好的規則一起工作時 , 它們就足以獲得所有利益 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	建議是 , 我們構想一個叫做 「 特區城市 」 的東西 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定規則開始 , 來吸引建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 來建造電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 他們會先僱用那些先搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家人 , 那些將來會永遠住在那裡的居民 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 找到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了那張憲章 , 人們就會搬到那裡去 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造起來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一而再、再而三地做下去 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了讓它成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	圖中所捕捉到的那些 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人民的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這其實是建立在模型上的如果我們能在無人居住的土地上建造城市
you start from uninhabited territory .	從無人居住的領土開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以生活在新的憲章之下 , 但沒有人會被迫活在它之下 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是為領導者做選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要領導者的那種選擇 , 我們需要讓各國之間的合作有潛力:國家之間的合作 , 實際上 , 中國和英國的合作方式 , 首先是建構市場模式的一小部分 , 然後再擴大到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 不經意地 , 英國通過香港的行動 , 減少了世界貧窮 , 比上個世紀所有援助計畫所做的更多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們能讓這樣的合作再次重現 , 我們就能讓全世界都受惠 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會牽扯到責任的代表權 , 從一個國家到另一個國家的代表權 , 來掌控某些特定的行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我說這句話時 , 有些人開始思考: 「 這是否只是帶回殖民主義 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是的 。 但很重要的是要意識到 , 當我們開始思考這些事情時所產生的情緒 , 可能會阻止我們退回來 , 會關閉我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的地方在於 , 在我們的一些援助計畫中 , 常常是不好的 , 它涉及到強制和優越的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式的重點在於選擇 , 不論是領導人 , 或為將來住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是強制和優越的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談它如何實踐 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	以一位特定的領導人raulcastro為例 , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定想到他有機會為古巴做到像鄧小平對中國做的事 , 但他沒有香港在古巴島上 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他的確在南方有一點點亮光 , 這裡有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣周圍有一塊區域 , 條約為美國政府負責一塊地 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚去找加拿大總理 , 說: 「 看 , 雅肯人有嚴重的公關問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不加拿大接管呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建立一個特殊的管理區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新的城市在那裡建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近有香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會支持 , 但這將是通往我國家的現代經濟和現代世界的通道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	那麼 , 這個模式還能在哪裡試驗呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我曾和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全了解特區的想法 , 認為人們可以選擇成為一條規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	它是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方式 , 讓人們不受強制 , 不受強制的反對 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下 , 他們能對長期投資者做出更有信心的承諾──將來會建造港口的投資者 , 在新城市中建造道路 , 如果他們能和另一個國家合作 , 他們就能做出更有信心的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許在某些安排中 , 有點像信託帳戶 , 把土地放在信託帳戶中 , 而合夥的國家要負起責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲還有許多可以建造新城市的土地 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在沿著海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣的大片土地 , 可以讓數億人居住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們將這個概念推廣到不只是一、二個特區 , 而是數十個城市 , 能夠幫助許多數億人 , 甚至數十億人搬到城市裡 , 有足夠的土地供給他們嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在世界各地 , 如果我們晚上看著燈光 , 有一件事是誤導人的 , 就是 , 視覺上看來 , 世界上大部分的人都已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	讓我告訴你們為什麼這是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以這個代表所有的土地為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個方形 , 代表地球上所有的可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表的是三十億人口居住的城市已經佔據的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到方形的底部你會發現現有30億的城市只佔了地球上可耕地面積的3%
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想為其他十億人建造城市 , 他們會是像這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們從百分之三的耕地 , 降到百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們大幅減少了人類在地球上的足跡 , 做法是建造更多可以移居的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市有良好的規則 , 就能成為城市 , 在那裡 , 人們能安全地從犯罪中、疾病 , 和不良的衛生設施 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以得到一些基本設施 , 像是電力 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要建造出第一座特區城市 , 要花什麼代價才能建造出更多的城市 ?
it would help to have a manual .	擁有一本手冊是有幫助的 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們可以做的就是寫一些細節 , 寫進這本手冊中 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們管理城市 , 出去設計城市 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者去野外 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們開始思考像這樣的問題 , 假設不只加拿大和拉爾•卡斯楚有關的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西也參加了 , 西班牙也希望古巴想成為四方聯合大企業的一員 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何訂定條約來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	之前就沒那麼先例了 , 但很容易就解決了 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何提供資金 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現新加坡和香港是靠在他們剛開始時所擁有的土地價值大增的城市 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地價值來支付像是警察、法庭等費用 , 但學校和健康照護體制 , 讓這個地方更吸引人 , 讓人們有更高的收入 , 順帶一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	因此 , 幫助建立這塊區域的人的動機 , 建立了基本規則 , 往正確的方向前進 。
so there are many other details like this .	還有很多類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何讓第一份工作的人負擔得起低成本且負擔得起的建築物 , 組裝iphone , 讓那些建築物的能源效率提高 , 確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會在地震或颶風中下降 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術細節尚未解決 , 但我們這些已經開始追求這些事情的人 , 已經可以分辨出沒有路障 , 沒有阻礙 , 除非想像失敗 , 否則我們無法實現真正的全球雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來總結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能這麼幸福 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現想法時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物體 , 分享意味著我們每個人都能取得更少的資源 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們以這種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類想法:規則主宰我們如何彼此互動的規則 , 比如 , 讓我們來設立一個稅收系統 , 來支持一個研究大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個系統 , 在那裡 , 我們有土地 , 可以登記在政府辦公室裡 , 人們可以保證它是相對的 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續創新我們的規則 , 尤其是創新的制度 , 來改變規則 , 我們就不會卡在不好的規則上 , 那麼我們就能持續進步 , 真正讓世界變得更好 , 讓尼爾森和他的朋友不再需要在路燈下學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	先驅克萊格•凡特從史詩級的圓形考察中休息一下 , 來談談數百萬個基因 , 他的團隊目前已經在探索要繪製海洋生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、遺傳學、海洋、科學、科技、科技等 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特在dna和海上航行 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	剛開始 , 我被幾個人問我關於老化議題的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這是我對此唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者比悲觀主義者活得更久 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內 , 我要告訴你們的是 , 我們將如何從解讀遺傳密碼轉換到開始自己寫程式的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅在10年前的這個月 , 我們發表了第一組完全沒有生命的有機體的基因序列 , 叫做嗜血桿菌 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了十三年的時間 , 縮減到四個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去十年間 , 大量的基因組被加上:大部分的人類病原體、幾株植物、幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳類 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	大約十年多前 , 基因組學的思考階段是在今年底 , 可能會有三到五組基因組的定序 ; 數百組的排序 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從godon和bettymoore基金會取得一項補助 , 到今年進行130組基因組定序 , 作為環保有機體的副產品 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 外頭有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有抓住地球上可用的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分人不知道 , 因為它們是肉眼看不見的 , 但微生物佔據了地球生物總量的一半 , 而所有的動物只佔了生物總量的一半 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許在牛津的人們不太常這樣做 , 但如果你去海邊 , 吞一大口海水 , 請記住每一毫升都有大約一百萬個細菌和一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	兩年前 , 只有不到五千種微生物種類被分類 , 所以我們決定要為此做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們成立了 「 足球三號探險 」 , 在那裡 , 我們進行了很棒的海洋探險 , 每200英里的一次採集樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始進行我們的測試計畫 , 接著搬到哈利法克斯 , 向下美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿越加拉帕戈斯 , 橫越太平洋 , 現在我們正在橫渡印度洋的路上 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的責任 ; 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 有一部分是要協助年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只是拿海水過濾 , 蒐集不同的大小生物 , 用不同的濾鏡 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 我們可以在24小時內完成一億個基因編碼的定序 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	通過這樣做 , 我們有了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 人們認為我們的眼睛裡有視覺色素 , 環境中只有一到兩種有機體有著相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎世界上溫暖地區的所有物種 , 都有相同的光感接收器 , 以太陽光作為它們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	一個地點 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬個新基因 , 多達5萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	現在我們用sloan基金會的補助金將它延伸到空氣中 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量我們每天呼吸多少病毒和細菌 , 尤其是在飛機上或封閉的會堂上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 我們從僅僅一天就在紐約市的一棟大樓上收集10億微生物的排序 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們目前正在進行排序 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	在資料收集方面 , 我們在加拉帕戈斯的位置 , 我們發現 , 幾乎每兩百英哩 , 海洋中的樣本就有極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些在邏輯上是合理的 , 就不同溫度層面來說 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 根據溫度紅色是溫暖的藍色 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現 , 溫暖的水樣和冷水樣本之間有很大的差異 , 就富足物種而言 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件讓我們相當驚訝的事就是這些感光受器能偵測到不同波長的光 , 根據胺基酸序列 , 我們能預測這些波長 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些變化非常大 , 從區域到區域都有 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外地 , 在深海 , 大部分是藍色的 , 感光器通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有很多葉綠素時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但在最極端的紅外線和紫外線有更多的變化 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了評估我們的基因庫是什麼 , 我們收集了所有的資料 , 包括遠離探險的所有資料 , 這代表了地球上超過一半的基因資料 , 總計大約有2900萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些放進基因家族中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現已知家族的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新的家族 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因族群 , 但我們在環境中所採取的每一種新樣本 , 都會對這些新家庭有一條線性時期 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	我們正處於關於基本基因、元件和生命的最早發現階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看到所謂的進化樹 , 我們就在右上角 , 和動物在一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在大約2900萬個基因中 , 我們的基因組只有24 , 000個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物放在一起 , 我們可能就共有不到三萬隻 , 也許還有十多種不同的基因家族 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認為這些基因現在不僅僅是演化的設計要素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為以基因為中心的角度來看或許回到richarddawkins的想法而不是以基因為中心的角度來看 , 這些基因組成的不同結構 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna的能力 , 能夠合成dna的能力 , 和過去十年或二十年間 , dna測序的速度差不多 , 變得越來越快、非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們對人造基因組的第一個想法是在1995年我們對第二組基因組進行基因組定序的時候 , 那是從我的血漿生殖器得到的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只是簡單地問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800種 , 再另外500種 , 是否有更小的基因組可以組成一個最小的作業系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始做轉位子突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉位子只是基因編碼中隨機插入的一小片dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果插入到基因的中央 , 就會阻斷它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張地圖 , 上面有所有能夠進行轉位子插入的基因 , 我們稱之為 「 非必要基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對此非常重要 , 你只能依據環境中的東西來定義一個必要或非必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也嘗試用比較直接的智能方法來處理13種相關的有機體基因組 , 我們試著比較它們 , 看看它們有什麼共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們找到了這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們找到的只有173個基因 , 適用於所有13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了一個細胞寄生蟲 , 這個池塘會再擴大一點 。 當我們觀察核心基因組的310左右 , 它會擴展得更多 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因組 , 依據你的觀點來看 , 到300到400個基因 , 從500的最小值 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法 , 就是用這些基因建立一個人造染色體 , 我們必須以一種模糊的方式來進行 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大片土地裡合成精確的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	史密斯和clydehutchison , 我同事開發了一個令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能在兩週內合成一個5000個鹼基對的病毒 , 以其序列和生物學而言 , 精確度高達100% 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一個相當令人興奮的實驗當我們把合成的dna注射到細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始促使病毒粒子轉向並殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個人造病毒 , 小兒麻痺病毒一年以前就被製造出來了 , 但只有十分之一的活躍 , 而且花了三年的時間才完成 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的結構圖 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這個例子是軟體現在建立自己的硬體 , 這是生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立刻開始關心生物戰事 , 最近我在參議院委員會前發表了證詞 , 美國政府設立了一個特殊委員會來審查這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 把現實放在心中是很重要的 , 而不是人們的想像會發生什麼事 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 今天任何已經完成基因序列的病毒都可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上會對伊波拉病毒或天花感到驚訝 , 但這種生物的dna沒有傳染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人製造天花的基因組 , dna本身不會引起感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正關心安全部門的問題是設計師設計的病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯有很大的努力想要創造生物戰爭代理人
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這項研究真的被終止了 , 未來的設計師病毒應該不會有太大的活動 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為在兩年內 , 單細胞生物就有可能發生 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能是真核細胞 , 那些我們擁有的細胞 , 在十年內就實現了 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在正在製作數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變這個人造染色體中的序列和基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你要如何把其他的都放在一起 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們先從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一個同源重組系統將這些碎片重新組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個生物體中衍生出來的 , 耐輻射可以容納三百萬拉德輻射 , 不會被殺 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆炸之後 , 它會在12到24小時內重新組合它的基因 , 在它的染色體被完全分開之後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這個有機體在地球上無所不在 , 可能因為我們的旅程 , 已經在外太空中存在了 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一座玻璃啤酒器 , 經過約50萬拉德輻射之後 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和破裂 , 而微生物坐在最底層 , 愈來愈開心 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張實際情況的照片上面的是經過170萬拉德輻射後的基因組
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體被炸開了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動組裝完成 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	令人驚訝的是 , 這些生物的確可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有數千種 , 甚至數萬種不同的物種能做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成之後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為人造細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅僅是為了了解生物基礎 , 同時也為了環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們所定序的第三個有機體中 , 甲烷-jannascii-它生活在沸騰的水溫中 ; 它的能量來源是氫 , 它從環境中吸收來的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 數以千計的生物 , 它們是從二氧化碳生長出來的 , 可以追溯回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其用從石油中取得的碳來進行合成過程 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 並從大氣中捕捉回來 , 將它們轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種從一氧化碳中生存的生物 , 我們把水分解成氫和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	還有很多路徑可以被改造成甲烷代謝 。
