and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦特有一項重大的計畫 , 用在挪威的石油來捕捉和將甲烷從天然氣田裡轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	不久之後 , 我認為會有一個新的領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些大量的基因陣列重組和同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 一天可以製造出也許一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有生物學一樣 , 你會透過篩選來選擇 , 不論是檢測氫化生產 , 或化學生產 , 或只是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因所扮演的角色 , 就會很容易取得 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用以直接從陽光生產氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節 , 我們認為有一種氧不敏感的氫化酶會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合纖維素 , 分解複雜糖分解的酵素 , 在同一個細胞中製造乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	使用微生物的藥物生產已經在大型實驗室中進行了 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物所產生的化學成分比我們最好的化學家所能產生的複雜程度還要高 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源、環境修復的來源 , 也許可以取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我以倫理和政策研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年延遲了實驗的開始 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 審查是否應該嘗試製造人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖使用他們的教義作為法律書 , 他們找不到任何東西禁止製造生命 , 所以這肯定沒問題 。 最終的擔憂是生物戰的方面的 , 但前提是我們要開始進行這些實驗的原因 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	史隆基金會剛剛資助了一份多機構的研究 , 來找出對社會有何風險和益處 , 以及像我這樣的科學團隊應該在這個領域中使用的規則 , 我們正試著建立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了威脅生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是很簡單的議題 , 我們能否設計東西來產生乾淨能源 , 也許能革新發展中國家的做法 , 並提供各種簡單的處理方式 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•辛巴多說幸福和成功是源於一種特質:我們對過去、現在和未來的方向有所忽略 。 他建議我們把時間校準在改善我們生活的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理學、科學、科學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利普津巴多開給健康的處方 , 準時的考驗 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密 , 短時間內的想法 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始時鐘 。 三十秒鐘工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	請保持安靜 。 安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	時間 , 結束序列 。 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、7、6、5、4、3、2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:讓我們調整一下亞當的誘惑原則的對話 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 亞當 , 不要那麼灰暗 。 咬一口 。 」 「 我做到了 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 。 不要放棄伊娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 各位 , 我不知道 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 , 一口 。 到底怎麼回事 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	人生是誘惑 。 重點是要產生、抗拒 , 是的 , 遲到 , 衝動、焦點 , 和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾的美德會落入當下的熱情中 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	少女承諾要在婚前保持性別疏離和處女 , 多謝喬治布希大部份 , 60% , 會在一年內對性誘惑產生影響 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	他們大多數都沒有採用避孕法 。
so much for promises .	許許多多的承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在 , 來試試四歲小孩 , 給他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們就可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 它會付出代價 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	發生的狀況是三分之二的孩子給予誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 , 其他人當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 。 他們延遲了現在 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特.米歇爾 , 我在史丹佛大學的同事 , 在14年後 , 試圖發現這些孩子的不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	兩種孩子之間有很大的差異 , 在抗拒的孩子和被大量產出的孩子之間 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	抗拒分數在sat上得分高了250分
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那是很大的 。 這就像一整套不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有惹上麻煩 , 他們是比較好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是有自信和堅定的 。 今天對我來說 , 對你來說 , 關鍵是 , 他們是以未來為中心 , 而非以現在為中心 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀點是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 如何把你的經驗分成時間區或時間類別 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動且無意識地去做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	不同文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育水平之間的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會變得有偏見 , 因為你會學會過度使用它們 , 並濫用其他的 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做一個決定 , 決定你要採取什麼行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 這只關乎當下的狀況 , 其他人的行為和感受 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	當這些人做決定時 , 會用這種形式來做決定 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現狀 」 , 因為他們關注的是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在並不重要 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是在說 「 我過去經歷過的情境是什麼樣子 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決策是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們稱這些人為 「 過去式 」 , 因為他們關注的是 「 過去式 」 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人 , 不是過去 , 不是現在 , 只關乎未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們關注的重點是預測結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們稱他們為 「 未來導向 」 。 他們關注的是未來式 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想說的是時間觀點的悖論 , 是會影響你做的每一個決定 , 你完全不知道 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有這種偏頗的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	嗯 , 其實有六個方法 。 有兩種方式可以呈現出來 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以懷疑 , 兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面的 , 或是負面的 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是 " 享受主義者 " , 也就是你專注於享受人生的樂趣 , 或是當今主義者--這並不重要 , 你的人生被控制住了 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來導向的 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:生命始於死後 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展思維的靈活性 , 來轉換時間觀點 , 根據情況的需求 , 這是你必須要學習的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳時光檔案 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度積極正面、高度適當的未來 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	並且適應當下的 " 現在主義 " 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低落於負面和現代主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以最理想的暫時性混合就是你從過去積極的過去中得到的 , 給予你根源 。 你將你的家人、身份和自我聯繫起來 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	從未來你能飛到新的目的地、新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從當下的享樂主義得到的能量 , 是探索自己的地方、人、感性的能量 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過渡時間的觀點 , 都有比正面更負面的觀點 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來要犧牲什麼才能成功 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間、犧牲朋友時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲快樂時光 , 犧牲個人的放逐 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲嗜好 。 他們犧牲睡眠 。 這會影響到他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們為了工作、成就和控制而活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我確信會和一些ted成員產生共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這讓我產生共鳴 。 我小時候在南布朗克斯貧民區長大 , 那是西西里島家庭 , 大家都住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來這裡是一位未來導向的人 , 走過頂端 , 犧牲一切 , 因為老師介入了我 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等你得到兩顆棉花 , 直到我學會了平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了 " 現在主義 " , 我把焦點放在 " 正面主義 " , 所以 , 在76歲的時候 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更開心 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們把這個應用在許多世界問題上:改變輟學率、對抗成癮率、增強青少年健康、用時間隱喻來治療退伍軍人的創傷後壓力症候群──取得神奇的解藥 , 促進永續性和保育 , 減少身體康復率 , 在那裡有50%的輟學率 , 改變自殺傾向 , 改善家庭衝突的時間軸 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以我想以此作結:生命中的許多謎題可以藉由理解你的時間觀點和他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 顯而易見 , 但我認為後果是非常深遠的 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	在一百年後 , 現今的頭條新聞會有多少關聯 ? 1000年 ? 柯林•凱特朗的 「 長期新聞 」 專案計畫收集現今不只關注數十年的新聞 , 還會共鳴數十年 。 在ted2010年 , 他強調了近期的頭條 , 有潛在的可能性 , 來塑造我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、科學 。
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的新聞 。
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞裡 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透社一年就刊出了350萬則新聞 。
that's just one source .	那只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:在長期來看 , 到底有多少故事是很重要的 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是一個長遠的現在基金會的計畫 , 由tedsters所創立 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華布蘭德 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的新聞報導可能在50、100或10 , 000年之後仍然很重要 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過過濾器看新聞時 , 很多東西會從旁邊掉下來 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	以去年p.的頂尖故事來說 , 這在十年內會很重要嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會有什麼影響嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 還蠻酷的 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但去年的頭條是經濟 , 我敢打賭 , 遲早 , 這個衰退將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事能為未來帶來改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 以科學為例 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小型機器人會穿過我們的血液串流來修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠 , 有一天你已經在這裡了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	有些最近的故事:奈米蜜蜂用真實的蜜蜂毒液把基因送到大腦中 , 一個可以在人體上爬行的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	現今 , 餵養六十億人是有問題的 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人在挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國若沒有修改過的作物 , 就會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲已經投入了十億美元在農業研究上 。
what about global politics ?	那全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	當中國設立議程時 , 世界將會變得非常不一樣 , 而且他們可能 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超過美國成為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超過德國成為最大的出口國 , 他們開始對孩子做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的事業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們在尋找各種方法 , 來回推動我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近一些發現:阿根廷有一個蟻群 , 已經散播到每個大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 有一個自我導向的機器人科學家很快地發現 , 科學很快就不需要我們了 , 生命也可能不再需要我們 ; 一個微生物在120 , 000年後醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎 , 有沒有我們 , 生命會延續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但我在過去一年中選出的長篇新聞 , 是這個:在月球上發現了水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	要把蟻群放在那裡容易多了 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不這麼做 , 中國可能會 , 或是在座的某個人可能會寫很大的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡羅琳•帕爾科秀了卡西尼航行到土星的圖片 , 焦點在它最大的衛星泰坦 , 以及冰凍的土衛二上 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa , 設計 , 探索 , 科學 , 太空 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 視覺化圖像化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco飛向土星
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	接下來的十八分鐘 , 我要帶各位踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這是一段旅程 , 你和我已經進行了很多年了 , 它從50年前開始 , 人類第一次踏出地球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年裡 , 我們不但真的登上了月球 , 我們還把機械飛行器送給所有八個行星 , 我們登陸在小行星上 , 我們已經對彗星重新發掘 , 此時此刻 , 我們有一艘太空飛船 , 前所知的星球 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械裝置的任務都是人類更大的旅程之一:一趟旅程 , 去了解事物 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 去了解我們的起源 , 了解地球 , 我們的星球 , 我們賴以生存 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中 , 所有我們想去的地方 , 尋找像這樣的問題的答案 。 這是土星 。 我們去過土星 。 1980年代早期我們去過土星 , 但我們對土星的研究都變得更加深入 , 自從卡西尼號太空船開始經過星際空間長達七年之久 , 在2004年的夏天 , 登上土星軌道 , 成為人類歷史上最遙遠的機械人 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘的、科學的洞見 , 以及顯然比對外的迷人光芒 , 而這個系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙能力 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究光環 , 我們就能夠學到很多關於恆星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這是andromedanebula美麗的照片這是我們銀河系中最接近最大的螺旋星系
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	接著 , 這是旋渦星系的美麗複合物 , 由哈勃太空望遠鏡所拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程 , 其實是一部分 , 也是一種比喻 , 象徵了更大的人類旅程 , 來了解我們身邊一切事物的關聯性 , 以及人類如何融入那張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位我們在卡西尼學過的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示我們過去兩年半所拍攝的美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我要把焦點放在這次重大探險旅程中最讓人興奮的兩件故事 , 我們在土星上進行探險 , 已經持續了兩年半了 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星與一大群多樣化的衛星同行 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小範圍從幾公里到大到像美國一樣 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們拍攝的土星大部分美麗的照片都伴隨土星 , 還有一些衛星 。 這是土星和土星 。 這是土星和土星 。 這是土星和土星 , 展示光環外圍的光環 , 向你們展示它們有多薄 , 垂直的 , 用土衛二 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	土星47顆衛星中有兩顆是站著的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六土衛六土衛六 。 土衛六是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼號到達之前 , 也是我們在太陽系中最大的一個未被探索的地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	這個身體長久以來一直引起許多關注 , 關注著這些行星 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它的大氣層非常厚 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為更像地球上的環境 , 至少過去 , 在太陽系中的任何其他身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層主要是氮分子 , 就像你在這裡呼吸的氮氣一樣 , 只不過它的大氣層被簡單有機物質包覆著 , 像是甲烷、丙烷、乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	泰坦大氣中的這些分子被分解後 , 它們的產品結合在一起 , 形成霧狀顆粒 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種霧狀物無所不在 , 它是全球性的、封閉的土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也是為什麼我們不能用肉眼可見的光譜來看到表面 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀顆粒在卡西尼號到達之前 , 經過數十億年的時間 , 緩慢地移向地表 , 覆蓋在厚厚的有機煙霧中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	像泰坦一樣 , 泰坦的油 , 油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以是土衛六表面溫度的液態 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是泰坦水對地球的影響 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是可以冷凝的 , 所以 , 要意識到這種情況 , 才能帶來一個奇怪的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在這些雲上方 , 有數百公里長的霧狀物 , 可以防止任何陽光進入地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	地表溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	儘管溫度很低 , 土衛六上還是會下雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上 , 降雨對地球造成的影響是:它會雕刻地殼 ; 它會形成河流和白內障 ; 它會形成峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和坑洞中游泳 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把泥土從高山的山峰和山坡上沖到低地 。 所以停下來想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它很暗 。 土衛六上的中午和地球上擦拭的深海一樣黑 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很邪惡 , 很可能會下雨 , 你可能會站在密西根湖邊 , 上面有顏料稀薄 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在卡西尼號到達之前所看到的土衛六表面 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在土衛六上發現了什麼 , 雖然它在細節並不相同 , 但它的迷人之處就跟那個故事一樣 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像是卡西尼人--這就像是叢林凡爾納的冒險成真 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有很厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這張照片是泰坦的背光 , 太陽的背光 , 光環則是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	還有另一個月亮 , 我甚至不知道是哪個月亮 。 這是個非常廣泛的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有儀器 , 能透過大氣層看到地表 , 我的相機系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你所看到的是明亮且黑暗的區域 , 差不多就是它為我們帶來的 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這真是太神秘了:我們無法弄清楚我們在泰坦所看到的 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你靠近這個區域 , 你會開始看到一些東西 , 像是一些我們不知道的 , 一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	我們後來發現 , 這其實是一個坑 , 但土衛六表面上只有極少數的隕石坑 , 意思就是 , 它是非常年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來像是構造 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來好像被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到一個星球上有線性的東西 , 它就意味著有裂痕 , 像一個斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它在地質上被改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 一件事情發生了 , 許多人認為卡西尼號是土衛六的高峰調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那是惠更斯探測器的部署 , 歐洲的惠更斯探測器在整個太陽系中運行了七年 。 我們把它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 它花了兩個半小時才降落 , 它降落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調這個事件有多重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的儀器 , 它第一次登陸在外太陽系 。 這是人類史上第一次 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	這實在是太重要了 , 在我心目中 , 這個活動應該要被美國和歐洲各個城市裡的滑行錄音帶遊行慶祝 , 很遺憾 , 事實並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這很重要 , 因為這是一個國際使命 , 這個活動在歐洲、德國被慶祝 , 而慶祝的演講被用英文口音、美國口音、德語、法語、義大利語和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是一場正在進行的演示 , 說明了 「 聯合國 」 應該要表達的意思:一個真正的聯合國團結起來 , 集合了一份巨大的努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 要探索一個星球是非常大的任務 , 要理解一個星球系統 , 這個系統在人類歷史上 , 一直是不可靠的 , 而現在 , 人類已經觸摸到了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我是說 , 我在談的就是雞皮疙瘩 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極度情緒化的事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記這件事 , 你們也不應該如此 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	總之 , 探測器對大氣層的測量進行了測量 , 並且拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 看到第一張泰坦表面的照片是怎樣的 。 這是我們看到的景象 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	那很震驚 , 因為那是我們希望其他照片從軌道拍攝到的 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	這是一個明確的圖案 , 一個地質圖案 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種樹突排水模式 , 只靠液體流動才能形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以遵循這些管道 , 你可以看到它們是如何匯合的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們聚集在這裡 , 流入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像是海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍攝的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在8公里高的地方拍的 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大概是航空公司的高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要乘飛機穿越美國 , 你會飛到這些高度 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這是你在土衛六航空公司的窗口所拍攝到的照片 , 當你飛越土衛六表面時 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器終於在地表上安息了 , 女士們先生們 , 這是第一個從外太陽系月球表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水冰鵝卵石 , 對嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在了其中一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 它沒有沉下 。 所以它不是我們著陸的流體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	基本上 , 探測器下降的情況等同於一片泥土平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一塊未整合的土地 , 被液態甲烷所包圍 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是因為這種材料已經從土衛六的高地上清洗過 , 穿過我們看到的這些管道 , 花了數十億年 , 來填補低窪的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但仍然 , 我們的影像中沒有標誌 , 或甚至在惠更斯的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	它們在哪裡 ? 當我們找到沙丘時 , 它更讓人困惑了 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們在土衛六區域的影片 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘有100公尺高 , 被幾公里的沙丘分開 , 延續好幾英里路程 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	那裡有數百個沙丘 , 高達一千到一千到一千兩百英里 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	這顯然是個非常乾燥的地方 , 否則你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	同樣的 , 這也讓人感到困惑 , 沒有任何液體 , 直到最後 , 我們看到了極地的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	土衛六南極有一個湖泊 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	它跟安大略湖差不多大 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	接著 , 一個禮拜半前 , 我們飛越了北極 , 發現了 , 同樣的 , 我們發現了加勒比海這麼大的一個特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以似乎液體 , 基於某些原因我們不明白 , 或至少在這個季節 , 很明顯地是鐵達尼號的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你們應該會同意 , 我們發現土衛六是一個不可思議、神秘的地方 。 它很奇特 , 但卻很像地球 , 擁有類似地球的地質構造 , 和一個巨大的地理多樣性 , 一個迷人的世界 , 它在太陽系中唯一與複雜及豐富的相互競爭 , 就是地球 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛六 。 土衛二是一個小衛星 , 大約是泰坦大小的十分之一 。 你可以在英國旁邊看到它 , 給你看看大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二是非常白的 , 非常亮 , 它的表面很明顯地破壞了 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它在地質上非常活躍 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二上的發現大多是南極發現的 , 我們現在看到的是南極 , 我們發現了破裂的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被覆蓋著 。 這些裂縫被有機物質覆蓋著 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個南極地區 , 溫度上升了 。 這是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這很奇怪 , 發現地球南極比熱帶地區還熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拍了額外的照片 , 我們發現 , 從這些裂縫中 , 會發射出微小、冰粒 , 延伸到太空中數百英里 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們將這張圖譜編碼出來 , 呈現出微弱的光度 , 我們可以看到這些噴射流進去的光譜 , 事實上 , 在其他影像中 , 我們可以看到 , 在土衛二上方數千英里的太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊研究了像這樣的圖片 , 像這張圖片 , 思考了卡西尼公司的其他成果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是這些噴射流可能是從土衛二表面下的液態水噴發出來的 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們有可能有液態水、有機物質 , 以及過多的熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們有可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 也就是說 , 一個適合生物生存的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我想我不需要告訴各位 , 在我們的太陽系中其他地方發現生命 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有龐大的文化和科學意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明創世紀已經發生了不止一次 , 而是在我們的太陽系中 , 獨立發生了兩次 , 那就意味著 , 根據推斷 , 它在整個宇宙中發生了無數次 , 且它的137億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是唯一一個充滿生命的行星 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它是珍貴的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 它依然是我們所知唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們當中有人在1960年代有警覺和連貫 , 我們會原諒你們 , 如果你沒有 , 好 , 你們會記得1968年由阿波羅八號太空人拍下的這張非常有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次從太空中拍攝地球 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置產生了巨大的影響 , 以及我們對於地球保護的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們在卡西尼號拍下了相同的照片 , 這是前所未見的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	這是日全食從土星的另一側看到的景象
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這個不可能的美麗圖片中 , 你可以看到主光環被太陽照射 , 你可以看到太陽被重新射出的影像 , 事實上 , 這個光環是由土衛二的排出物形成的 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這還不夠聰明 , 我們可以在這個美麗的影像中發現我們自己的星球 , 塞滿了土星光環的臂彎 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 看到我們自己從遠處移動 , 捕捉到我們在其他星球的天空中的小藍色的行星 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而那 , 我們從中得到的觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這個發現的旅程中得到的最好的獎賞 , 大約是半個世紀前 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到2005年 , 世界僅有15%的人被繪製出地圖 。 這減緩了災難後的援助 , 隱藏了未使用土地和未知道路的經濟潛力 。 在這簡短的演講中 , 谷歌已故的卡達示範者 , 全球各地的人用繪製地圖繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、技術 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	最近 , 卡塔格達:繪製地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 颶風納吉斯摧毀緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人急需幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要趕人和供應給這個地區 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有辦法幫助受害者到達氣旋的地圖 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 我們很難相信在2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地區被繪製在可數位化的細節上 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國也把世界大部分的民眾臉孔視為一個問題:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但救命來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 40位志工用新軟體繪製出12萬公里的道路 , 3000間醫院 , 運輸系統和救援點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一項科技 , 讓每個人能夠繪製我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從道路到河流、學校、當地企業 , 和影片商店到轉角的商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名人hernandodesoto發現 , 對大部分開發中國家來說 , 經濟利益的關鍵是要利用大量未破壞的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 光是在印度 , 就有數兆美金的房地產尚未被記錄下來 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 170個國家中數以千計的使用者就已經繪製出了數以百萬計的資訊 , 創造出了一幅從未想過的細節地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這一切都是因為熱情的使用者無所不在的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在讓我們來看看使用者製作的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 當我們說話時 , 這裡有170個國家的人正在繪製世界地圖 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑剛繪製了塞內加爾的道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家近一點 , 查盧亞 , 班加羅爾的g路線 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學、手勢識別和機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者的勝利 , 數百個城市、一個使用者、一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是對70%未被開發的星球的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村落建立了一個長達10個月的非暴力抗議活動 , 來阻止他們在橄欖叢林裡建起一道障礙 。 你聽說過嗎 ? 不這麼想 。 巴西的電影製作人朱利亞•巴查問為什麼我們只關注以色列衝突中的暴力 , 而不是非暴力領袖有一天會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、影片、和平、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:注意非暴力行為 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去八年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人試圖用和平的方式來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 總是有一個問題:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 我通常才剛從中東回來 , 我拍攝了數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力的方式來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和移民者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者正試著要打造一個大規模的非暴力運動 , 來終結該區域的佔領 , 並建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這兩者之間的差異 , 即發生在地面和國際觀念之間的差異 , 也是為什麼我們還沒有一個巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動成功的原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以我今天來這裡是要談關注的力量 , 你的關注的力量 , 以及非暴力運動在西岸、加薩和其他地方的興起和發展 , 但今天 , 我的個案研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 非暴力發展所缺少的 , 並不是巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段 , 而是我們開始注意那些已經是誰 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我帶你到一個叫布德鲁斯村的村莊來闡述這個觀點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈要建造一個隔離屏障 , 其中一部分的障礙會建在村子上 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 被包圍住 , 這樣他們就能免費取得剩下的西岸 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地受到鼓舞的領導 , 他們發起了和平抗爭活動 , 來阻止這種事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 你們可以明白地面上到底是什麼樣子的 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知牆會將巴勒斯坦與以色列分開 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村 , 我們意識到牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人:這道圍籬其實已經為恐怖創造了解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請去和平遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十位以色列兄弟姐妹加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列抗議人士:沒有什麼比非暴力反對者更害怕 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但他們沒有人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們能做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須清空我們傳統思維的空白 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯政黨成員:我們完全和諧 , 我們想要把它傳播到巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	口號:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔 , 哈馬斯和大眾前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主播:圍籬的衝突持續著 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被派來散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男人:這些是活的子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像法魯吉 , 到處開槍 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列抗議人士:我確信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但 , 我身邊有其他人甚至沒有求愛 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭不會阻止這場戰爭 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	口號聲:我們做得到 ! 我們做得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞•巴查:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體沒有報導這一系列非凡的事件 , 發生在七年前 , 2003年 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更讓人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民在十個月的和平抗爭後說服了以色列政府將這道障礙從他們的土地移到綠線上這是國際公認的以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗藥性從此流傳到西岸的村落 , 到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然對這些故事很冷靜 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默對非暴力發展的可能性造成很深遠的影響 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦 , 巴勒斯坦能夠生存下來 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭有一項非常重要的共通點 ; 它們都是某種形式的劇場 , 想要讓觀眾致力於他們的理想 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果只有暴力的人才會得到頭版 , 並吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦問題 , 對非暴力領袖來說 , 很難向他們的社區證明公民不服從是可行的選擇 , 來處理他們的困境 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能對在座的父母一點都不意外 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	讓你的孩子越來越大聲丟出的最好方法就是讓他第一次把注意力丟出去 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	反覆思考會變成童年心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子知道他能從中得到父母的關注 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以透過給予孩子注意力或戒斷來鼓勵或抑制他們的行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但這也適用於成人 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為會受到影響 , 取決於國際社群選擇聚焦在哪裡 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終結中東的衝突的核心 , 將和平帶給我們 , 是要把非暴力行為轉變成功能性行為 , 做法就是讓大家更注意現今在地面上的非暴力領導人 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝我的影片到西岸、加薩、東耶路撒冷的村落中 , 我見識到就算只有一部紀錄片也能影響轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做瓦拉吉的村落 , 位於耶路撒冷的很靠近 , 這個社區正面臨著和布德鲁斯村非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去許多土地 , 失去自由 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用非暴力手段兩年了 , 但自從沒人注意到他們之後 , 他們開始變得不高興 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們安排了一個篩檢 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們舉辦了目前為止最完善且有紀律的示威 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民看到布德鲁斯村的故事被記錄在電影中 , 覺得確實有人在追蹤他們所做的事 , 人們在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列這一邊 , 有一個新的和平運動叫做slidariot , 意思是希伯來語中的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者一直把布德鲁斯村當作主要的招募工具 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說 , 以色列人以前從來沒有活躍過 , 看過影片後 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰和索里德拉蕊運動的例子顯示 , 即使只有一部小成本的獨立電影也可以扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力轉變成功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 如果大型媒體開始報導每週發生的非暴力示威遊行 , 像比利、尼林、瓦拉耶 , 在耶路撒冷的鄰里 , 像謝赫賈拉和絲綢 , 非暴力領袖會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們就隱形了 , 就好像從來沒有發生過一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但是我親眼見過如果我們這樣做 , 它們會相乘 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們倍增他們的影響力會在以色列和巴勒斯坦的衝突中成長
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力就是那種能夠終於解開局面的影響力 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明了非暴力是可行的在布德鲁斯村 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們把注意力交給他們 , 讓他們可以證明它無所不在 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•桑克有個簡單但強大的模式 , 能鼓舞人心的領導力都從金色圈開始 , 問 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁•路德•金、萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	野牛、商業、企業家、領導、銷售、銷售、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•正恩克:偉大的領袖如何啟發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你如何解釋當事情不如我們預期 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的是 , 你要如何解釋當其他人能夠達成似乎違反所有假設的事物時 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 比他們所有的競爭對手都更有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 它們只是一間電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	它們和其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才能 , 同樣的機構 , 同樣的顧問 , 同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有所不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德金恩領導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受到公民權益困擾的人 , 他肯定不是當時唯一偉大的演說家 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出掌控、動力強的飛行器 , 當有其他團隊更有資格、更好的資金時......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有成功 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有別的東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我有了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作方式的看法 , 甚至深深改變了我運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大、具啟發性的領導人和組織 , 不論是蘋果電腦、馬丁路德金或是萊特兄弟 , 他們都會用同樣的方式來思考、行動和溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這完全和其他人完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是將它編碼 , 它可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圓 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 如何 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小想法解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導人能夠啟發其他人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上的每一個人 , 每一個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百知道他們在做什麼 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不論你稱之為你不同的價值觀提案 , 或你的私人訴訟程序或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或機構知道他們為什麼要做這些事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	我所謂的 「 為什麼 」 並不是指 「 賺取利潤 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 , 總是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	所謂 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的目標是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果就是 , 我們思考的方式、行為的方式、我們溝通的方式 , 都來自外在 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 。 我們從最清楚的東西 , 轉變為最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但 , 鼓舞人心的領導者以及鼓舞人心的組織 , 不論它們的大小 , 不論它們的產業都會從內而外去思考、行動和溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果是因為它們很容易懂 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果跟其他人一樣 , 他們的行銷訊息可能聽起來會像這樣: 「 我們製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很容易使用 , 且很友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? 「 我 」 。
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是多數行銷的方式 , 多數銷售都是這樣完成的 , 而多數人際溝通就是這樣 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們所做的 , 我們說我們如何不同 , 說我們如何更好 , 我們期待某種行為 , 購買 , 投票 , 諸如此類 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律事務所:我們有最好的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是為和我們一起做生意的客戶做生意 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很大的汽油里程 , 有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這是蘋果電腦溝通的方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是 , 把我們的產品設計得很漂亮 , 很容易使用 , 且很友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好做了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同 ? 你準備好向我買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	這證明了人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你的為什麼 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每一個人都可以完全舒服地從蘋果買一台電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很自在地買蘋果的mp3播放器 , 或是蘋果電腦的電話 , 或是蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如我之前所說 , 蘋果電腦只是一間電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	結構上沒有任何區別他們與任何競爭者的差別 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣有資格製造這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出平面電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們有資格製作平面電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們已經做平面監視器好幾年了 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾發明了mp3播放器和pda , 他們做出了很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美設計的產品 , 沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 現在我們已經談過了 , 我們甚至無法想像從戴爾電腦購買mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會買電腦公司的mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和所有需要你的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和那些相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我跟你說的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	這都是基於生物學的基礎 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看一下人類大腦的剖面圖 , 從上往下看 , 你看到的是人腦其實是分成三個主要元素 , 與黃金圈完美地相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人 , 我們的新皮層 , 會對應到 「 什麼 」 的層次 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責我們所有的理性、分析的想法和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部份組成我們的邊緣大腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責所有的感受 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以理解很多複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、好處、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它只是不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內而外的溝通時 , 我們正直接對著控制行為的大腦說話 , 然後我們允許人們去合理它 , 用我們說和做的有形事物 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是勇氣決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你會給人所有事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道事實和細節是什麼 , 但感覺不太對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	我們為什麼要用這個動詞 , 它不 「 感覺 」  ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的腦部區域並不控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	而我們最能忍受的就是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時候你會說你在帶領你的心 , 或你在帶領你的靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	我很不想對你們說 , 這些不是身體的其他部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	一切都發生在你的大腦邊緣 , 控制決策 , 而非語言的那部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你要做你該做的事 , 人們會回應你為什麼要做你該做的事 , 那麼你要如何才能讓人們為你投票 , 或向你買東西 , 更重要的是 , 要忠實 , 想要成為你所做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是要賣給需要你所擁有的人 ; 目標是要賣給那些相信你所相信的人們 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要雇用需要工作的人 , 而是要雇用那些相信你所相信的事的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你雇用員工 , 只因為他們能做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的事的人 , 他們會用血、汗、淚水來為你工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有其他地方比萊特兄弟更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分人不知道samuelpierpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初 , 追求有權力的人機就像當時的網路公司一樣 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpierperpontlangley曾經擁有過 , 我們認為是成功的秘訣 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或你的公司會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是會給你同樣的三件事:不足、不適合的人、不適的市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	這三樣東西都是一樣的 , 所以讓我們來探索一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley得到了5萬美金的戰爭部門 , 來找出這個飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	錢也沒問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉辦了一座座椅 , 在史密森尼亞工作 , 他認識了當時的所有人 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的人才資金 , 市場狀況也很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑 , 每個人都支持蘭利 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那我們為什麼從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley呢 ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	離俄亥俄州的幾百英里遠 , 奧維爾和威爾布萊特 , 他們沒有任何我們認為的成功的秘訣 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 ; 他們用自行車店的程序來支付他們的夢想 ; 萊特兄弟的團隊中沒有任何一個人有大學教育 , 連歐維爾或威爾堡都沒有 ; 紐約時報也沒有跟隨他們到處去 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 奧維爾和威爾伯被一個目的、一個目的、一個信念所驅使 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這台飛行機器 , 就能改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不一樣 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要變得富有 , 他想要成名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊特兄弟夢想的人用血汗、汗水和淚水和他們合作 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人則只是為薪水工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們講述的故事是 , 每次萊特兄弟出門時 , 他們都得要採取五組零件 , 因為那是他們出門前會墜機的次數 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	直到1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟開始飛行 , 甚至沒有人可以體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後 , 我們發現了這件事 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步證明langley被錯誤的動機所驅使:萊特兄弟起飛的那天 , 他放棄了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 各位 , 那是個驚人的發現 , 我會改善你們的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他放棄了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你的信仰 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的信仰的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人們很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一個叫做創意的散播法則如果你不知道這個法則你一定知道這個術語
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	前2.5%的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們早期採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你早期的大多數、已故的多數人 , 及已故的後代 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人購買觸控電話的唯一理由 , 就是因為你不能再買轉子手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在各種地方 , 在不同的時間 , 在這個尺度上 , 但創新的擴散法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場的成功或大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你就不能擁有它 , 直到你在15%到18%之間達成這個臨界點 , 然後系統就會崩解 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新企業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡跟你說: 「 喔 , 這大概是10%吧 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以讓客戶超過10% 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的人 「 明白 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	我們就是這樣描述他們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是那種直覺 , 「 喔 , 他們就是懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:在你和他們做生意之前 , 你要怎麼找到那些無法得到它的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	正如jeffreymoore所說的 , 就是這個小小的缺口所謂的 「 跨越鴻溝 」 , 因為 , 大部分早期的嘗試都不會先嘗試直到別人嘗試 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期採用者 , 他們對於做出這些膽量的決定感到很自在 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們會更自在地做出這些直覺性的決定 , 由他們對世界的信念所驅動 , 而不僅是產品的可得性 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排隊排了六個小時 , 第一次出櫃時 , 買了一支iphone , 下週你只要走進商店就買了一支手機 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面電視上 , 第一次上映 , 即使這項技術是不可或缺的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順道一提 , 他們並不是因為這項技術太棒 , 他們為了自己而做 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	那是因為他們想要成為第一名 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做的事只會證明你相信什麼 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做的事來證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	人們買iphone的原因是在前六個小時排隊排了六個小時 , 是因為他們所相信的世界 , 以及他們想要每個人如何看iphone:他們是第一位 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗以及一個有名的成功案例 , 關於創意的散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 知名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如我們先前所說 , 第二 , 成功的秘訣就是金錢 , 正確的人和對的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該要在那之前成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從tivo出版時期到今日 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手放下 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們的資金非常好 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場的條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我總是把東西放在垃圾時間華納dvr上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是個商業上的失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們上了ipo , 他們的股票價格大約是30到40美金 , 然後就下跌了 , 從來沒有在10美元以上交易過 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它是在六歲以上交易的 , 除了幾個小突點之外 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個產品可以暫停現場的電視節目 , 跳過廣告 , 重新學習現場電視節目 , 記下你的收視習慣 , 而且你連問都不問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	憤世嫉俗的多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 。 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你嚇到我們了 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全掌控你生活的各個層面的人 , 孩子 , 我們有這個產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場的電視節目 , 跳過廣告 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼只是證明你相信什麼而已
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你一個成功的例子關於創意的散播法則
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 25萬人出現在華盛頓的購物中心聽金恩博士演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有寄出任何邀請函 , 也沒有網站去查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	該怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一位偉大的演說者 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一一個遭受過預防權利的人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些點子很差 。
but he had a gift .	但他有份禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們 , 什麼需要改變美國 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他到處告訴人們他相信什麼 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	相信他所相信的人們把他的理想拿走 , 他們讓理想變成他們自己的人 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 來讓更多人接受這個詞 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	你看 , 25萬人在適當的日子出現 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為了他而出現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了自己而出現 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們所相信的美國 , 讓他們能在八月中期站在華盛頓的陽光下旅行八個小時 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人和白人:百分之二十五的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信 , 世界上有兩種法律:那些由更高權威制定的法律 , 和那些由人所制定的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	除非所有人類定律和更高權威制定的法律一致 , 否則我們會活在一個正義的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	正好如此 , 民權運動才是幫助他實現理想的最佳辦法 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順道一提 , 他發表了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	聽聽現在的政治人物 , 用他們全面的12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的位置 , 但領導的人鼓舞了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們追隨領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們追隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 有能力可以啟發他們周圍的人 , 或找到能激勵他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記住你車子的位置 ? 你怎麼知道你是往正確的方向移動的 ? 神經科學家neil大量研究我們身邊空間的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結記憶和想像 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburges:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在大型停車場停車時 , 我們怎麼記得我們停車的地方 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這是荷馬面對的問題 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們會試著去了解他的大腦發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 以黃色顯示 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你的車子受到損傷 , 就像阿茲海默症一樣 , 你記不得東西 , 包括你停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是拉丁文的 「 海馬 」 , 和它的名字很像 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元組成 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人腦內有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元通過互相連接傳遞電脈衝或電突突突突來彼此溝通
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片非常密集的細胞組成 ,
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的藉由記錄老鼠在尋找食物時的個別神經元或老鼠的記錄
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	想像一下 , 我們正在記錄這隻老鼠的海馬體神經元 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一小波電時 , 會有一個紅點和一個點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以我們看到這個神經元知道老鼠在環境中的某個特定位置 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	藉由發送電刺激 , 傳送訊息到大腦的其他部位 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以讓神經元的發射率作為動物所在位置的函數 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們紀錄許多不同的神經元 , 我們會發現當動物在不同的環境中移動時 , 不同的神經元會發射出訊號 , 就像這個方形的方形盒子裡的一樣 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 它們一起形成了一張大腦的地圖 , 持續地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中的哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被人類記錄下來 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以 , 癲癇患者有時需要監測腦部的電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	其中一些病人玩電玩遊戲 , 他們在小鎮上開車到處跑 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬體中的位置細胞會發射、活化、開始發送電子脈衝 , 每當他們開車經過某個特定的小鎮時 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個位置細胞如何知道環境中的老鼠或人在哪裡 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的邊界非常重要 。
