so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	上方的那一隻會在老鼠的箱子牆之間發出訊號 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你把盒子擴大 , 發射位置就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的這棵樹每當有一面牆接近南方時就會發火
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放進盒子裡 , 細胞就會在南方的任何一面牆上被激發 , 因為動物會在盒子裡四處探索 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這項預測能感應到你周圍的邊界和方向──擴展建築等等──對海馬體來說是特別重要的 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在對海馬體的輸入資料中 , 發現了哪些專案計畫進入海馬體 , 確切反應出偵測邊界或邊緣 , 特別距離和老鼠的方向 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 每當動物接近一面牆 , 或是向東邊界線 , 不論是方形的箱子的邊緣或圓形的牆 , 或是圓形的牆 , 或甚至是桌子的邊緣 , 動物在周圍移動 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞每當有界線到南邊時就會被激發不管是桌邊或是牆壁或是兩張桌子間的縫隙都被拉開
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以 , 我們認為位置細胞能決定動物在四處探索的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也能測試我們認為物體的位置 , 例如這面旗幟 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或者 , 你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以 , 我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 去觀察他們必須記住的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放回到環境中 , 它們通常很擅長把標記放到他們認為旗幟或車子的地方 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們對位置細胞所做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這個例子中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置是如何改變的 , 改變了環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 你看到的國旗是方形空間中那個交叉點的位置 , 如果你問人們它在哪裡 , 但你讓環境變大了 , 他們認為旗幟的位置和位置細胞被激發的地方是一樣的 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好像你還記得旗幟的位置 , 透過儲存位置細胞各處的激發模式 , 然後你就可以藉由四處走動 , 以便找到符合目前位置細胞激發的模式 , 以儲存位置的圖案 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想要記住的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道 , 透過運動 , 我們在哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們沿著一些邊界的路徑走 , 也許我們停了下來 , 我們就會知道 , 因為我們自己的動作 , 我們可以整合這個路徑 , 大概就是我們要回去的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會得到這種路徑整合的訊號 , 來自一種叫做格子細胞的細胞 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞再次被發現 , 輸入海馬體 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個細胞會在一系列不同的位置激發 , 以驚人的三角形網格呈現 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你紀錄好幾個格子細胞 , 這裡有不同的顏色 , 每個格子的激發模式在整個環境中有類似的激發模式 , 而每個細胞的激發模式 , 都和其他細胞稍有不同 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的會在這個網格上發射綠色的 , 藍色的在這個網子上 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 綜合在一起 , 老鼠可以在環境中放置一個虛擬的網格 , 有點像地圖上找到的緯度和長途線 , 但用的是三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電子活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 以追蹤它的所在位置 , 這樣它就可以用它自己的動作來知道它在環境中的哪個位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	由於所有類似網格的發射模式都有相同的對稱軸 , 如同格子的位置 , 在橘色的位置 , 這表示 , 所有網格的活動 , 都應該根據這六個方向來改變 , 或是在中間的六個方向之一來運作 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放進核磁共振儀中 , 讓他們做一個電玩遊戲 , 就像我剛給你們看的那個 , 並且尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 在人類的腦皮層也就是老鼠腦內的網格細胞
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能記得他的車子在哪裡 , 以距離和方向 , 來延伸建築物和界線 , 在他停車的地方 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	那會被邊界偵測細胞的激發來呈現 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他走出停車場的路 , 公園會在網格細胞激發時被呈現出來 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞被激發 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以藉由移動來返回停車位的位置 , 找到目前在他腦中位置細胞的激發模式 , 與他停車的車子停車位的位置相匹配 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那引導他回到那個位置 , 視覺提示的位置 , 像是他車子是否真的在那兒 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被用完了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡取得它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找類似網格的激發模式 , 我們會在一系列的位置上看到它 , 當我們進行各種自傳記憶任務時 , 會很活躍 , 比如說 , 你上次去參加婚禮時 , 會記得它 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 也許是神經機制 , 代表我們身邊的空間 , 也能用來產生視覺圖像 , 讓我們能創造出空間的場景 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像時 , 發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果發生了 , 你的記憶可以從位置細胞開始 , 透過密集的互相連結來啟動彼此 , 接著再啟動邊界細胞 , 創造出你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個視角 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種我還沒提到的頭部方向細胞 , 它們就像是指南針 , 根據你面對的方向 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義觀看的方向 , 例如你想要為你的視覺影像產生影像 , 你可以想像你在婚禮上會發生什麼事 , 比如說 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是認知神經科學的新時代的一個例子 , 我們開始了解心理學過程 , 像是你如何記得、想像、甚至思考 , 以數十億個獨立神經元所組成的大腦所採取的行動 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 一個全球安全的驅動力 , 是由政府部門、私營部門和大眾合作所驅動的 。 這不是遙遠的開放原始碼的希望 , 而是北大西洋的詹姆士史達維里迪斯的願景 , 他是北約最高層的指揮官 , 他們在近代軍事歷史上分享了鮮明的活力 , 來解釋為什麼未來的安全性應該要用橋樑來建造 , 而不是用牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放原始碼、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史瓦里迪斯:北約最高指揮官如何看待全球安全 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我將要談的是開放資源的安全性 , 因為我們在21世紀得更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先說 , 讓我們回顧二十世紀 , 了解安全的風格對我們是如何運作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 法國的戰場就在北約總部的比利時 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在verdun , 在超過300天的期間 , 70萬人被殺 , 一天大約2000人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它往前推進二十世紀安全進入第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到史達林格的戰役 , 300天 , 有兩百萬人被殺 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續建造圍牆 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的壕溝走到第二次世界大戰的馬基諾線 , 然後我們走進冷戰、鐵幕、柏林圍牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的論點是 , 與其建造圍牆來創造安全性 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲一座知名的橋 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	這是在愛佛•安德里的河上方的橋樑 , 也是愛佛•安德里的小說主題 , 它談到歐洲和巴爾幹半島的這部分 , 長久以來一直有巨大的牆壁 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在過去十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫地 , 團結起來 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我認為 , 同樣地 , 開放式安全是關於聯繫國際、跨部門、私人公共 , 並以戰略性溝通 , 主要是以社交網路 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為全球公有物正受到各種攻擊 , 而對全球公有物來說 , 沒有任何威脅的來源可以通過築牆 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	很顯然 , 我是水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一條線 , 橫越印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它沿著邊緣有協奏曲線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	那是為了阻止海盜攻擊 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	海盜是現今全世界非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	海盜在馬拉卡海峽也很活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它在幾內亞灣活躍 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海也看到了 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	它是全球交通運輸系統的一百億美金不連續性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 當時有20艘船 , 500名船員持有人質 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要思考如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉移到另一種海洋 , 網路的海洋 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩個年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	此刻 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一個信用卡詐欺 , 將他們網上超過一百億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是全球經濟損失2兆美元的網路犯罪的一部分 。
two trillion a year .	每年兩兆美元 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是英國的國內生產毛額而已 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以 , 我們所知道的網路海洋是最基本的開放性 , 也受到很大的威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	在全球公有物中 , 我擔心的另一件事 , 是被人口販賣所造成的威脅 , 由毒品、鴉片等運動所造成的 , 從阿富汗穿過歐洲到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心來自安第斯山北邊的可卡因 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器的運輸 。 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人口販運 , 以及它的成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣主要是在海上 , 但在全球公有物的其他地方 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你們 , 這是美國海軍的高科技設備 , 用來阻止販運 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是毒品販毒集團執行的半潛水員 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它是建在南美叢林裡的 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那個低科技的木筏捕捉到牠 , 牠載著六噸可卡因 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四人組成 。 精密的溝通掃除了 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販運 , 在毒品、人、武器、神禁止 , 在大規模毀滅的武器中 , 是威脅全球公有物的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	咱們來看看今天在阿富汗的狀況 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的一片餅乾 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上百分之八十到九十的狗、鴉片和海洛因來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	當然 , 我們也看到了恐怖主義
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這就是基地組織建立的地方 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到了非常強的叛亂隱藏在其中 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 這種恐怖主義擔心也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須要處理的是什麼 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以現在我們來到21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道20世紀的工具是行不通的 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我認為我們不能僅僅靠槍支來遞送安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會僅靠槍支來遞送安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這麼做時 , 我們必須做得很好 , 且要有競爭力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放式安全是關於國際、跨部門、私人和公共的聯繫 , 由這種在網際網路上戰略溝通的概念所拉扯 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子來說明這是如何運作的 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 , 我想我讀到在阿富汗的人口統計、年輕人和女性 , 大多是不識字的 。 」
you would be correct .	你是對的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	當他們進入阿富汗的安全部隊時 , 百分之八十五無法閱讀 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班在這些男人和女人學會閱讀的時期 , 保持著高等教育 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們在教導他們閱讀讀北約的讀寫課程 , 與私人企業合作 , 與發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教導了超過二十萬的阿富汗安全部隊 , 以基本的層面去閱讀和寫作 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你能在阿富汗讀和寫的時候 , 你通常會把一支筆放在口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在儀式中 , 當這些年輕人畢業時 , 他們帶著自豪的筆 , 放進他們的口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	國際間有50個國家參與這項任務--跨部門--這些發展機構和私人公共 , 來對抗這種安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也在教他們戰鬥技能 , 但我認為 , 開放式安全意味著連結 , 創造出更持久的安全效應 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做舒適感 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一艘叫做慈悲的姐妹船 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院的船隻 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這個 , 舒適的是整個加勒比海和南美洲的海岸進行病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	在一般的航程中 , 他們會做四十萬名病人治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	船員不是嚴格的軍隊 , 而是結合人道主義組織: 「 希望 」 、 「 微笑 」 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織派遣志願者 。
interagency physicians come out .	跨學科醫生出來 。
they're all part of this .	他們都是這方面的一部分 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	給你一個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲的小男孩 , 帶著他的媽媽走了兩天 , 來安慰舒適的眼科診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他被適應時 , 在他的極端神秘眼睛上 , 他突然抬頭說: 「 媽媽 , veoelmundo 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽媽 , 我看到世界了 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	將這個乘以40萬的病人治療 , 這個私人的合作與安全部門合作 , 你就會開始看到創造安全的力量以非常不同的方式 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你看到的是棒球員 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能在照片中挑出兩位美國軍人嗎 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是這兩位年輕男孩的一邊 。 這是棒球診所的一部分 。 我們在全美大聯盟棒球隊 , 國務院裡 , 探討了合作 , 他們設立了外交部 , 軍事棒球員 , 他們是真正的士兵 , 但參與了這個任務 , 他們在拉丁美洲和加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比 , 加勒比海 , 加勒比 , 所有中美洲的棒球隊 , 都是真正的士兵 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它向年輕男女展示關於健身和生活的榜樣 , 我認為可以幫我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	這種合作關係的另一面是災難救援 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是一架美國空軍直升機在2004年投入海嘯後 , 殺害了25萬人 。
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在這些重大災難中 , 2004年的海嘯 , 25萬人死亡 , 2005年巴基斯坦的卡什米大地震 , 8萬5千人死亡 , 海地地地地震 , 30萬人死亡 , 更近期 , 地震海嘯的組合震撼了日本和核能產業 , 在所有這些例子中 , 我們都看到了國際間的合作關係 , 跨部門、跨部門合作 , 和安全性合作 , 來對抗這種自然災害 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	這些都是開放原始碼安全的例子 。
we tie it together , increasingly , by doing things like this .	我們將它綁在一起 , 透過這樣的方式 , 逐漸地 , 我們將它綁在一起 。
now , you're looking at this thinking , " ah , admiral , these must be sea lanes of communication , or these might be fiber optic cables . "	現在你看到的這個想法是: 「 啊 , 司令德 , 這些必定是通訊的航線 , 或者這些可能是光纖電纜 。 」
no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不 , 這是twitter所畫的圖像 。
purple are tweets . green are geolocation .	紫色是推特綠色是地理位置
white is the synthesis .	白色是合成 。
it's a perfect evocation of that great population survey , the six largest nations in the world in descending order: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .	它是人口調查的完美提升 , 全球六大國家以下順序:中國、印度、臉書、美國、推特和印尼 。
why do we want to get in these nets ?	為什麼我們要用這些蚊帳呢 ?
why do we want to be involved ?	我們為什麼要參與其中 ?
we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們先前談到了阿拉伯之春 , 和這一切的力量 。
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉一個例子 , 它是如何傳遞這個訊息的 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦發表過類似這樣的演講 。 我說 , 如同我對你們說的 , 我在臉書上 , 朋友 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	觀眾笑了一下 。
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	有一篇文章在電線上由ap來經營 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	世界上有兩個地方:芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	標題是:北大西洋公約需要朋友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	這個故事是催化劑 , 隔天早上我收到數百個臉書朋友請求 , 來自印尼和芬蘭 , 他們大多說: 「 承認 , 我們聽說你需要一個朋友 , 喔 , 順道一提 , 哪個是北約 ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	是的 , 我們會笑 , 但這就是我們如何傳遞訊息 , 將訊息傳遞出去 , 就是我們如何連結國際、跨部門、公共和國 , 以及這些社會網絡 , 來協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我來談談一個嚴肅的話題 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這是勇敢英國士兵的照片 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭警衛隊 。
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他在helmand , 在阿富汗南部 。
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我讓他來這裡提醒我們 , 我不希望任何人離開房間 , 認為我們不需要有能力、有能力的軍隊 , 來創造真正的軍事效應 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	這就是我們是誰的核心 , 我們做的事是保護自由 , 言論自由 , 所有我們在社會中珍視的東西 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但 , 你知道 , 人生不是開關 。
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要在戰鬥中 , 要麼在戰鬥中 , 要麼在戰鬥中 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我會說 , 生命是隨機的 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你必須調節它 , 正如我所想的 , 我們該如何在21世紀創造安全 , 有時候我們會用真正的戰爭和危機來實施硬實力 , 但會有很多例子 , 如同我們今天所說的 , 我們的軍隊可以成為創造21世紀安全的一部分 , 國際安全 , 跨部門 , 私人 , 和密切的溝通 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後 , 我會說我們今天稍早聽說過維基百科 。 我經常使用維基百科來查看事實 , 如同在座的各位所知 , 維基百科不是被十二位傑出的人所封鎖在房間裡寫文章 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科 , 每天有數萬人在輸入資訊 , 每天有數百萬人在提取資訊 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	對我們所有人一起思考的基礎觀點來說 , 這是一個完美的圖像 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 我們沒有一個人像我們一樣聰明 , 一起思考 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的宣言很簡單:在這個世界裡 , 每個人都可以自由地分享所有知識 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是 , 透過結合國際、跨部門、私人、策略性溝通 , 同心協力 , 在21世紀 , 我們就能創造出所有安全的總和 。
thank you very much . thank you . thank you .	非常謝謝 。 謝謝 。
